Current Commentary

How Loyal and Brave is General Ma Zhanshan!

On September 18th, the Japanese army's violent act broke out suddenly. Hundreds of thousands of soldiers in our Northeast, armed and carrying weapons and responsible for defending the country, all retreated in disarray under orders not to resist, watching dozens of cities from Shenyang downwards and tens of millions of people fall into the trampling hooves of the brutal army in a matter of days. The exposure of this kind of cowardly situation has deeply saddened us and caused us great distress. The spirit of our country and the life of our nation have been almost completely lost by these people, leaving our nation with endless shame.

At this time, there is one General Ma Zhanshan of Heilongjiang. Based on the duty of a soldier, with the bloodiness of a man, with the loyalty of loving the country, with the spirit of disregarding success or failure and not fearing death, he led a lone army to fight a desperate battle with the Japanese brutal army that invaded our province of Heihe. In the Battle of the Nenjiang Bridge, General Ma personally went to the front line to command the battle. The entire army was inspired by loyalty and fought desperately. One fell, another stepped into the breach. In the end, they were able to defeat the brutal army, making them know that our country still has soldiers who can fulfill their duties. This kind of heroic war to win glory for the nation is truly moving and worthy of praise. It is truly enough to put to shame the ordinary soldiers who did not resist and fled. However, according to the current situation, the Japanese army is still continuously increasing its reinforcements. General Ma, with his isolated army without any support, will ultimately not be able to hold out for long. But even this is enough to show General Ma's loyalty and bravery. The general is not unaware that the connection with Jiang Province has been cut off, that calls for support have not been answered, and that a lone army in a corner is not enough to defeat ferocious tigers and wolves. However, inspired by loyalty and righteousness, he does not fear death. In his telegram, the General stated: "Zhanshan has a responsibility to defend the territory. As long as there is a breath left, I will never allow even an inch of land to be lost to foreign races." He also said: "I have the responsibility to defend the territory. I should give my life on the battlefield and vow to fight to the death with the enemy and never return alive." Alas, this kind of sincerity is enough to move heaven and earth and make the gods weep. Even if Qiqihar is unfortunately lost in the end, it will only be a normal thing in the victory or defeat of military strategists. How loyal and brave is General Ma! How tragic and heroic is General Ma!

Our country spends more than 80 percent of the national budget on the army every year, supporting more than two million soldiers. However, at this time, with a great enemy at our doorstep and the country in danger, they have not been able to fulfill their duty to defend the country and protect the people. Now that we have this model of unwavering loyalty in General Ma, they should also know how to strive and know how to emulate. Let us not blame the past, but look forward to the future. The people of the country should now wait and see what happens next.

Domestic Important Telegrams Two

Foreign Ministry Issues League of Nations Telegram

(Nanjing) The Foreign Ministry released a telegram from League of Nations Secretary-General Drummond from Geneva stating, "To the Nanjing Foreign Ministry, in accordance with the instructions of the Chairman of the Executive Yuan, please forward the following telegram for your information: 'On November 6th, I, the Chairman, telegraphed to both the Chinese and Japanese governments through your office. Now that I have received replies from both governments, I, the Chairman, extend my gratitude to both governments through your office. After careful study of the replies and recent documents received, I believe I should solemnly declare again that both governments have previously promised to do their utmost to avoid any actions that would expand the situation. I, the Chairman, also strongly urge that the officers in command of the confronting armies be strictly ordered to refrain from any new actions. Finally, I, the Chairman, believe it is of utmost importance that facilities be provided to the inspection personnel sent by the member states of the Executive Yuan to the area, especially those sent to the Nenjiang Bridge and Angangxi to gather information as stipulated in the resolution of September 30th.' Chairman of the Executive Yuan, Briand. (13th Dispatch)"

Foreign Ministry Telegraphs League of Nations Welcoming Neutral Personnel Investigation

(Nanjing) On the 11th, the Foreign Ministry received a telegram from League of Nations Secretary-General Drummond relaying a telegram from Briand stating that no new actions should be taken and requesting that facilities be provided to the investigation personnel. The Foreign Ministry has now telegraphed a reply to the League of Nations Secretary-General, welcoming an investigation by neutral personnel, and requesting that it be forwarded to Mr. Briand. The text of the telegram is as follows: "The Chinese government has received Your Excellency's telegram forwarded yesterday from the Chairman of the Executive Yuan, and is very grateful to learn that Mr. Briand continues to be extremely concerned about the current situation in the Far East. The Chinese government, apart from having no choice but to take necessary defensive measures against further deliberate attacks by Japan, will strictly avoid any military actions. However, the current situation is becoming increasingly serious due to Japan's continued expansionist actions. For example, at the Nenjiang Bridge in Heilongjiang Province, the Japanese army is concentrating and has declared its intention to seize the provincial capital, Qiqihar. Its commander even demanded that Chairman Ma of the provincial government hand over political power to Zhang Haipeng, a traitorous leader who is cooperating with the Japanese army. Furthermore, recently the Japanese have been engaging in various secret disruptive conspiracies in various parts of China. The events that have already occurred in Tianjin are entirely the result of Japanese planning and direction, and the Japanese barracks and concessions are being used as bases for their disturbances, causing even greater anxiety among Chinese and foreign people. Under these circumstances, the Chinese government sincerely hopes and welcomes neutral observers to go to the areas where the Japanese army is operating in order to obtain accurate information, especially to the Nenjiang Bridge and Angangxi in Heilongjiang, and to Tianjin and other important locations. The Chinese government will provide all necessary facilities to the observers to enable them to complete their tasks. Please forward the above documents to the Chairman of the Executive Yuan."

Shi Zhaoji Reports to the League of Nations on Japanese Seizure of Mines and Private Fabrication of Deeds

(Geneva) Chinese Chief Representative Shi today reported to the Council that the Japanese authorities sent small squads of soldiers carrying machine guns to forcibly seize important mines of the Northeast Mining Company, and dispatched Japanese personnel as advisors to various locations of the company, forcing Chinese employees to continue working under Japanese management, mining 250,000 tons of anthracite coal annually. He requested that Council President Briand ask the Japanese government to instruct the Japanese ambassador to return the company's mines to their legitimate original owners, so as to prevent the situation from becoming more serious. He also stated that the Japanese military authorities had previously taken blank documents from the Liaoning and Jilin provincial government offices, and are now privately filling them out to issue land deeds and mining licenses, thereby furthering the Japanese plot to seize property. In Shenyang alone, more than two thousand landowners have lost their property without cause. For example, the Xinghe Agricultural Society (transliteration) is one of the organizations created after the Japanese army occupied the area. Recently, after enclosing land, they notified the original Chinese landowners that if they cultivated the society's land without permission, they would have to sign new contracts with the society within a specified period, otherwise the land would be rented to others. Thus, the Japanese occupation not only expands the occupied areas, but also increases Japanese private property. While claiming to protect the lives and property of Japanese residents, they initially used Mongol bandits and other unscrupulous elements, and added Japanese advisors to various banks and business organizations, thereby undermining the original Chinese organizations and local governments. Later, they seized salt taxes, destroying foreign debt guarantees, and now they are forging land deeds, etc. (12th National Telegram)

British, American and Japanese Representatives Discuss the Dong Province Incident in Preparation for Attending the League of Nations

(Beiping) According to foreign sources, London reports that British Foreign Secretary Simon, US Ambassador Dawes, and Japanese Ambassador Matsudaira held an important meeting on the 12th, as a preliminary to the Executive Yuan meeting in Paris on Monday. The three discussed the Manchurian incident at the Foreign Office for about an hour and a half. Although the content was not announced, it is believed that it will greatly influence the determination of their respective governments' policies at future meetings. (13th Dispatch)

◎ London British Foreign Secretary Simon, US Ambassador Dawes, and Japanese Ambassador Matsudaira met at the Foreign Office tonight for an hour and a half to discuss the Liaoning-Jilin incident in preparation for attending the League of Nations Council. The content of the discussions is unknown, but according to reliable sources, the conversations were extremely frank. (12th National News Agency Telegram)

◎ London It is heard that after US Ambassador to the UK Dawes arrives in Paris tomorrow, key figures will conduct very important discussions with the Chinese and Japanese diplomatic representatives. Japanese Chief Representative Yoshizawa is currently in Paris. Chinese Chief Representative Dr. Shi will arrive on Saturday or Sunday. British Foreign Secretary Simon will also arrive in Paris on Sunday. Reuters has learned that Matsudaira may attend the Executive Council meeting with Yoshizawa. (12th Reuters Telegram)

Shi Zhaoji Submits Emergency Note to the League of Nations Reporting Honjo's Ultimatum

(Geneva) Chinese Chief Representative Shi today sent an emergency note to the Council, reporting that Japanese Army Commander Honjo sent a written ultimatum to Ma Zhanshan, the acting chairman of Heilongjiang Province, this afternoon, demanding that the Heilongjiang provincial government resign and immediately cede Qiqihar. He requested that Briand immediately intervene to prevent the Japanese army from taking further military action, stating that the Japanese are now about to occupy Qiqihar and the Tao'ang Railway. The Chinese army led by General Ma Zhanshan has retreated to Shanshanfang (transliteration), 17 miles from Dasing Station. Dasing Station is currently occupied by the Japanese army. If the Japanese continue to advance in violation of their commitments to the Council, a major war could break out at any time. Before sending the emergency note, Chief Representative Shi had informed League of Nations Secretary Drummond that the situation at Nenjiang was extremely dangerous, and that 4,000 Japanese soldiers were advancing on General Ma Zhanshan. At 10:00 p.m. on the 10th, several Japanese aircraft bombed Chinese military camps, killing and wounding several soldiers. Shi and Drummond discussed the matter for about 40 minutes in the evening, and afterwards stated that he had notified the League of Nations Secretariat of the most serious news, that the Japanese army, after reinforcements arrived, had sent an ultimatum to General Ma Zhanshan, threatening to attack with full force. (12th National News Agency Telegram)

(Geneva) Today, Chinese Representative Dr. Shi reported to the League of Nations Secretariat that Japanese Army Commander Honjo sent an ultimatum to Ma Zhanshan at noon today, ordering him to immediately withdraw from Qiqihar. The Chinese troops have retreated to Sanzhenfangzi, which is now occupied by the Japanese army. He requested that Council President Briand immediately restrain Japan. If the Japanese army carries out the intentions recently expressed by the Japanese government to the Executive Council, war will break out at any time. Council President Briand issued a note to China and Japan, urging them to respect their promises and refrain from any actions that would aggravate the situation. He also stated that the Executive Council will send personnel to Manchuria for inspection, and that both sides must provide all kinds of facilities. Geneva observers believe that the proposal to send personnel for inspection is a key diplomatic move, and the direction of next week's Executive Council meeting can be gleaned from this. Because the reports from both sides differ, and the members of the Executive Council seem unwilling to adopt coercive measures, in this situation, the intervention of a neutral party to investigate can save the critical situation and prevent the expansion of the war. China has now prepared for the arrival of inspectors. Dr. Shi stated that the Chinese Reception Committee was established on November 1st, with Gu Weijun as the chairman, to discuss the withdrawal of troops from the three northeastern provinces with Japan. The Chinese committee will request that representatives of the great powers cooperate closely with the Chinese committee. Dr. Shi also issued a document accusing the Japanese of forcibly seizing Chinese mines and land. The Japanese representative today sent a document to the League of Nations Secretariat, describing the banditry in Manchuria in great detail, stating that in order to effectively protect Japanese residents living in the interior, the existing force of 14,400 men is insufficient, so it is necessary to withdraw the Japanese and Korean residents along the railway into safe areas. However, many Koreans are unwilling to abandon their agricultural products and prefer to remain in their original locations. In order to perform its duty of monitoring the situation and protecting residents, the Japanese army has no choice but to station troops outside the railway zone at Zhengjiatun, Juliuhe, and other places in Jilin, and dispatch detachments from these three locations when necessary to drive out bandits and scattered soldiers. The railway zone is wide, so it is necessary to dispatch armored trains and aircraft. However, the Chinese claim that the Japanese aircraft are flying bombing missions, intending to sensationalize world opinion. The Japanese document also stated that the Chinese authorities are using bandits to attack the Japanese railway, causing the Japanese great losses. Since the incident in September, banditry has become rampant. From mid-September to October 27th, there have been a total of 577 bandit attacks. In addition to detailing the banditry in various places, the Japanese document also includes statistics. (12th Reuters Telegram)

Japanese Government Replies to Briand's Note, Shifting Responsibility for the Nenjiang War

(Tokyo) Regarding President Briand's new note yesterday urging avoidance of hostile acts, Foreign Minister Shidehara today instructed Mr. Sawada, Director-General of the Japanese Bureau, to reply to Mr. Briand as follows: The Japanese troops stationed near the Nenjiang Bridge have received instructions not to expand military operations if the Chinese troops do not engage in combat. This point was clearly stated in my reply to Your Excellency the President on November 8th. The following events have been repeatedly reported by the Japanese Director to the Council: the Chinese side has concentrated forces more than ten times greater than the Japanese army in Qiqihar, Angangxi, and south of there. I would like to draw Your Excellency the President's deep attention to this kind of threat to the Japanese army. The Japanese government can provide the Council with various information in accordance with paragraph 7 of the September 30th resolution. Japan will provide as much convenience as possible to the officials of the Council members who go to Manchuria for inspection after the occurrence of this incident. However, as mentioned above, Japan's attitude has not changed in the slightest. (13th Japan United News Agency Telegram)

Japan Reinforces Shenyang and Demonstrates with Artillery Fire in Shenyang

(Beiping) Japanese troops are being reinforced in Shenyang. The origin and destination are unknown. On the 11th, the Japanese army suddenly collected self-defense police guns, but it is said that they were returned, with each person given only two bullets. The Japanese army has been demonstrating with artillery fire in Shenyang for several days, and inspections of pedestrians are very strict. (14th Telegram)

(Harbin) The Shenyang Maintenance Association moved to the provincial government on the 10th and held a ceremony. Yuan Jinkai gave a speech. The Kwantung Army headquarters dispatched a chief of staff to deliver instructions. (13th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) A Harbin telegram stated that General Shirakawa, who was sent by Japan to inspect the Northeast, received important orders from the Ministry of the Army, and first dispatched Colonel Imai, the chief of the Second Section of the General Staff Headquarters, back to Tokyo, carrying a letter to Minister of the Army Minami, stating that as a result of the inspection, the Japanese troops stationed in the Northeast were extremely fatigued due to the rampant bandits and plainclothes teams, and requested that troops be increased immediately. Minami replied that troops would be increased after the army exercises were completed. (13th Central News Agency Telegram)

Japan Increases Air Force Strength in Dong Province

(Tokyo) The military authorities today ordered the air corps to quickly dispatch aircraft to Manchuria to replenish the aircraft destroyed by Chinese artillery fire, so as not to weaken the air force in Manchuria in the slightest. (13th Reuters Telegram)

Japanese Residents Leave Manzhouli

(Manzhouli) Because of rumors of war here, people are in a state of panic. Since yesterday, Japanese residents, women and children have been leaving here for South Manchuria, because it is said that General Ma Zhanshan has vowed to fight the Japanese army. The trains on the Chinese Eastern Railway still pass through Hailar and Angangxi to Harbin. Japanese residents, women and children leaving the country can only do so this way. (13th National Telegram)

Soviet Policy Remains Unchanged, Russian Newspaper Denies Imperialist Rumors

(Moscow) The Russian newspaper Rabochaya today stated that Russia is only adopting a policy of observation and neutrality regarding the Sino-Japanese dispute. The newspapers of British, American and French imperialism, disregarding Russia's categorical denials, are still spreading rumors that Soviet Russia is sending troops to Manchuria to help the Chinese army. It is important to know that the Soviet working class is now closely monitoring the events in the Far East. The Russian people do not want war, but are prepared to deal harshly with provocateurs. (12th Reuters Telegram)

Under Japanese Influence, Bandits Run Rampant in Jilin Province

(Beiping) A person from Jilin reported that the opinions of the provincial committee members below Xi Qia are quite inconsistent. Bandits are running rampant in the counties. For a time, there was a rumor in Yushu, Shulan, and Panshi counties that there were no virgins or chaste women in the villages on both sides of the road. Yitong County was captured by bandits on the 5th and is still occupied. The fierce bandit Zhongliexia sank a Dehui County warship on the Songhua River, drowning more than 130 members of the security team. The temporary office of the Jilin Provincial Government will be moved to Bin County. The 34th Regiment of Ma Zhanhai's troops has arrived there to defend it. The director of the education bureau has appointed Rong Mengmei to serve. Xi Qia is currently recruiting soldiers. About a thousand people have responded, all wearing yellow serge military uniforms, military hats, and red hatbands. At first glance, they almost look like Japanese soldiers. They are named the Garrison Team and stationed at the old site of the 34th Regiment outside Deshengmen. (13th Dispatch)

German People React Negatively to Eastern Newspaper Republishing Okuma's Essay

(Berlin) Recently, the Japanese Times published an essay by former Japanese Prime Minister Okuma. The essay was written by Okuma in 1921 and was published in newspapers. It stated that Japan's request that China recognize the Twenty-One Demands was originally intended to prevent China from joining the German-Austrian alliance in the European War. Berlin opinion is quite angry and surprised by the reprinting of this essay. Berlin political circles have declared that Okuma's remarks are groundless. Chinese President Yuan Shikai did not collude with Germany or Austria, and the exchange of correspondence with the former German Kaiser was because Qingdao and the entire province of Shandong were already in Japanese hands, so even if China wanted to join Germany and Austria, it would have been impossible. Moreover, Yuan Shikai repeatedly proposed to the Allies that China declare war on Germany and join the Allies, but the Allies ignored it. Today, it is pointless and ridiculous to try to link the Twenty-One Demands incident to Germany's political actions during the European War. (12th National News Agency Telegram)

Shenyang Security Association Establishes Autonomous Guidance Department

(Harbin) The Shenyang Security Maintenance Association has established an Autonomous Guidance Department, with Yu Chonghan as the director. Yu issued eight principles of autonomy: 1. Follow the will of the people; 2. Cultivate the strength of the people; 3. Treat everyone equally; 4. Practice incorruptible politics, with high salaries to foster integrity; 5. Each county should send personnel to the province to study autonomy; 6. Organize public security associations and recruit public security teams to suppress bandits; 7. Make finances public and establish an audit office; 8. Save expenses and reduce harsh taxes. This department is equivalent to the Department of Civil Affairs. (13th Dispatch)

South Manchuria Railway President Arrives in Shenyang to Prepare for Implementation of Concrete Policies

◎ Dalian South Manchuria Railway President Yasuya Uchida has discussed the concrete implementation of the fundamental policies toward Manchuria with government authorities and is confident. Tonight, he will take the night train to Shenyang with Vice President Eguchi. It is reported that after President Uchida arrives in Manchuria, he will begin preparing active concrete plans to resolve the outstanding issues in Manchuria. The economic issues centered on the Bank of the Three Eastern Provinces will also undergo fundamental reforms. (12th Japan United News Agency Telegram)

(Shenyang) South Manchuria Railway President Uchida arrived here this morning and immediately visited Kwantung Army Commander Honjo for an important meeting. (13th Japan United News Agency Telegram)

Japanese Residents in Hankou Intensify Street Fighting Exercises; Japanese Residents in Chinese Areas All Move to Concessions; Veterans Rush to Register; Unit Headquarters Establish Ordnance Repair Shop

(Hankou) Japanese residents in the Chinese areas all moved into the Japanese concession before the 13th. The Japanese authorities held a secret meeting, which was changed to be held at the Marine Corps headquarters. The Japanese Youth Corps is intensifying street fighting exercises, and the situation is extremely serious. (13th Dispatch)

(Hankou) Zhou Zechun, a diplomatic inspector of the five provinces, formally sent a letter to the foreign consulates stationed in Hankou on the 13th, requesting that if the Japanese use the methods of destroying the Northeast and Tianjin again to destroy Hankou, they should express their sympathy to China when necessary. (13th Dispatch)

(Hankou) Ishikawa Katsutoshi, in the name of the Hankou branch chairman, urgently informed the veterans stationed in Hankou to prepare their resumes and register quickly. Also, Japanese on the Japanese ship Shinyo Maru provoked an incident in Shashi on the 10th, but it did not lead to a major event. (13th Dispatch)

(Hankou) The Japanese Marine Corps headquarters has established an ordnance repair shop, which is contracted by the Sakurai Iron Factory. It seems to have ambitions for an uprising. Japanese residents from the upper reaches of the Yangtze River and from Changsha and Wuxue have all been ordered to come to Hankou or go to Shanghai. (13th Dispatch)

Bandits Rampant Along the South Manchuria Railway

(Harbin) Banditry is rampant along the South Manchuria Railway, and the Japanese army is quite troubled by the bandits. The number of bandits in each group is more than a thousand for large groups, and six or seven hundred for smaller groups. Currently, there are large groups of bandits in Haicheng, Sipingjie, Kaiyuan, Tieling, Xinmin, and Dashiqiao. The Xiaobailong gang is attacking Gongling. The Japanese garrison transferred a large team to defend on the 11th. (13th Telegram)

League of Nations Secretariat Sends Personnel to China for Liaison

(Nanjing) According to outside sources, the League of Nations Secretariat has specially dispatched an official, Henry Schuller, to China to represent the League of Nations and make close contact with the Chinese Foreign Ministry. (13th Dispatch)

Representatives of the Northeast People Request to Join the Reception Committee

(Nanjing) Representatives of the Northeast People's Petition Group suggested to the authorities that Northeast people's organizations be included in the Northeast Reception Committee to avoid separation. They have prepared a written opinion and submitted it for inspection. (13th Dispatch)

Dutch Lawyer Discusses League of Nations Resolutions

(Nanjing) A telegram from The Hague stated that the Dutch lawyer and League of Nations representative, Mr. Lamber, declared that the resolution passed by the League of Nations Executive Council on the 24th of last month regarding the Dong Province incident should be considered unanimously passed without any doubt. He also said that since Japan is recognized as a permanent member of the Executive Council and is also the President of the International Permanent Court, it should not arbitrarily abandon public law and betray its covenant. (13th Dispatch)

Japanese Warships Anchor in Shimonoseki

(Nanjing) Two Japanese warships arrived in Shimonoseki today, one was the Hirado, which came from Wuhu, and the other was the Tenryu, which came from Shanghai. Both are anchored in the waters of Shimonoseki. (13th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) On the morning of the 13th, a Japanese Hirado cruiser sailed from Hankou and anchored in the waters of Shimonoseki. (13th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Navy ordered Chen Xunyong, commander of the training fleet stationed in Shanghai, to lead his team to Beijing to defend it. The defense of Shanghai will be undertaken by the Chen Jiliang troops of the original First Fleet stationed in Xuzhou. (13th Dispatch)

US Ambassador Johnson Meets with Li Jinlun

(Nanjing) US Ambassador Johnson visited Acting Minister Li Jinlun at the Foreign Ministry on the morning of the 13th and left after talking for about half an hour. (13th Dispatch)

Swedish Chargé d'Affaires Negotiates Detention of Matches

(Nanjing) The Swedish Chargé d'Affaires visited Acting Minister Li at the Foreign Ministry at 11:00 a.m. on the 13th to negotiate the detention of matches by anti-Japanese associations in various places and left the ministry at 12:00 p.m. (13th Dispatch)

Hankou Garrison Strictly Maintains Local Security

(Hankou) The police department issued a notice on the 13th, stating that the diplomatic situation is serious and local security is important, and that the people should be orderly and abide by order, and strictly agreed on three matters: 1. Those who are hired and bought by thugs, using the name of patriotism, to engage in subversion, will be killed without pardon. 2. For those laborers who have been laid off by foreign companies, their unresolved legitimate issues should be reported to the competent authorities for negotiation. Those who directly negotiate and cause diplomatic incidents will be sentenced to death. 3. Meetings and associations must be approved by the headquarters and reported to the police department, otherwise they will be dissolved on the spot or detained. (13th Dispatch)

Chaoshan Declares Martial Law

(Shantou) Martial law has been declared in various counties of Chaoshan since the 7th. The division headquarters issued a notice stating that foreigners passing by at night must carry lanterns, stating their name and address. Each lantern is only allowed for one foreigner and one Chinese person. No more than three people are allowed to walk at the same time within 20 meters of each lantern, in order to facilitate inspection. (13th Dispatch)

(Shantou) Peng Jingyi, the magistrate of Meixian County, because refugees from the Jiangxi border continue to arrive in Meixian, convened various organizations to discuss: 1. Telegraph to the superiors to request instructions on whether to refuse or accommodate them; 2. The county party headquarters telegraphed the headquarters to send troops to support Jiangxi. The Jiangxi natives association in Mei issued a notice to register the refugees. (13th Dispatch)

Chen Jitang, Li Zongren, Tang Shaoyi, Deng Ziru, Bai Chongxi, and more than a hundred others went to the station to welcome them to Tuisiyuan for rest. Tianjin Student Delegation Petitions the Fourth Plenary Session, Received by Secretary-General Ye Chucang

(Tokyo) Approximately 300 students from various schools in Tianjin, including the Faculty of Law and Commerce, Women's Normal College, Vocational School of Fisheries, Rotary Middle School, Zhenzhong Middle School, Zhongshan Middle School, Jiuzhen Middle School, and Nankai Middle School, organized a petition delegation to petition in Nanjing. Today (the 13th) at 11:00 AM, they gathered at the Central University to petition the Fourth National Congress. Five representatives were first selected to explain their intentions to the staff of the Congress's Public Relations Section. Subsequently, they were received by Secretary-General Ye Chucang, and the representatives presented the main points of their petition and provided detailed explanations: (1) Organize a unified government to jointly resist foreign aggression; (2) Establish a National Defense Conference to consolidate national sovereignty and territory; (3) Actively prepare for war against Japan; (4) Enforce economic severance and order local governments not to interfere; (5) Restore the people's movement; (6) Expand international propaganda to achieve the goal of uniting with other nations in the world who treat us equally to fight together; (7) Based on the spirit of governing the country by the Party, delineate the powers of the Party, government, and military; (8) Clearly stipulate the people's legal obligations and rights and guarantee them; (9) Concentrate national talents. They also inquired about the simultaneous holding of the Fourth Plenary Session in Nanjing and Guangzhou. Finally, they requested the central government to (1) order the authorities in Hebei and Tianjin not to obstruct or resist the movement to boycott Japanese goods; (2) severely punish historical traitors; (3) move the deposed Emperor Puyi away from the Japanese concession in Tianjin to prevent him from being used by the Japanese. After the representatives finished their presentations, Ye Chucang stood up and replied, stating that before answering, two points should be clarified: (1) He was responding in his capacity as Secretary-General of the Congress; (2) The requests would be presented to the Presidium for submission to the Congress. He mentioned that some of the points raised were already being addressed by the Congress. The previous Shanghai talks had yielded results on the principles for improving Party affairs, government administration, and diplomacy, which had been disclosed in the newspapers and were known to everyone. As for the holding of the Fourth Plenary Session in two locations, it was a compromise by the central government to find the best way to end past disputes and achieve the goal of peaceful unification. The central government had initially hoped to hold it together, but the Guangdong comrades disagreed, so it was held separately. However, if everyone's sole purpose was to save the country, even if the Congress was held separately, the results would converge because the Shanghai talks, the Fourth Plenary Session, and the future Fourth Central Executive Committee were all moving towards the realization of a unified government. The organization of the National Defense Conference was, in principle, the government's duty, but the detailed arrangements could not be answered immediately. Restoring the people's movement and expanding the people's movement were essentially the same thing, and in fact, it had already been restored. Furthermore, if Japan did not comply with the League of Nations' resolution to withdraw its troops by the 16th of this month, further measures would be taken, which went without saying. As for the previous propaganda work, it was indeed not done well, but this time, there seemed to be more materials available, which was better than before, but not yet satisfactory. The representatives' suggestion was not so much a petition as a lesson to them. Regarding the issue of unification, they would spare no effort to make concessions to achieve it. Ye then went outside to meet with all the students and praised their spirit of enduring hardship and their patriotic fervor. Subsequently, everyone shouted in support of the Fourth National Congress of the Chinese Nationalist Party and then departed. (13th Dispatch)

Wang Jingguo and Others Go South to Attend the Fourth Plenary Session

(Beiping) Wang Jingguo, Sun Chu, Jing Yuexiu, Li Shengda, and others left for Nanjing today to attend the Fourth Plenary Session. Wang stated that the main points of the Shanxi-Suiyuan proposals roughly included matters such as border defense in Mongolia, developing the Northwest by migrating people and establishing borders, and completing the Baotou-Ningxia railway. Li stated that the troops under his command were stationed around Pingding, Yangquan, and Shouyang, and that the September salaries had already been distributed. Sun stated that the Shanxi Local Pacification Supervision Office was being organized with three sections: staff, adjutant, and military law, with a very simple structure, dedicated to commanding the provincial garrison to pacify the countryside and suppress bandits. Jing stated that he was representing the Shaanxi army at the Fourth Plenary Session and had yesterday met with Vice-Commander Zhang, who inquired in detail about the situation in the Northwest. (13th Dispatch)

Domestic Important Telegrams Three

Preparatory Meeting of the Fourth Plenary Session Held Yesterday, All Representatives Paid Respects at the Mausoleum Before the Meeting, Dai Huisheng and Others Elected to the Presidium

(Nanjing) At 7:00 AM on the 13th, all representatives of the Fourth Plenary Session paid respects at the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum. The ceremony included (1) standing in solemn silence, (2) paying the highest respects to the portrait of the Premier, (3) presenting wreaths, (4) observing three minutes of silence, (5) paying respects in the memorial hall, and (6) paying respects again to the portrait of the Premier. After the ceremony, they returned to the Congress venue to hold a preparatory meeting. Yu Youren presided and nominated candidates for the Presidium, proposed by the Central Standing Committee: Dai Huisheng, Pan Gongzhan, Enkebaatar, Huang Musong, Zhang Jiong, Mei Gongren, Zheng Zhannan, and Hu Boyue. The voting results were: Dai Huisheng 227 votes, Pan Gongzhan 211 votes, Huang Musong 161 votes, Enkebaatar 154 votes. The four were elected to the Presidium. (Note: The Congress Presidium consists of nine people, five of whom have already been appointed by the Central Executive Committee: Chiang Kai-shek, Dai Jitao, Yu Youren, Lin Sen, and Cai Yuanpei.) (13th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Fourth Plenary Session is scheduled to hold its second preparatory meeting on the morning of the 14th. (13th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) As of today, a total of 342 representatives have registered to attend the Fourth Plenary Session. (13th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) At 7:00 AM on the 13th, all representatives of the Fourth Plenary Session went to the Premier's mausoleum to pay respects. Central Committee members Chiang Kai-shek, Yu Youren, Dai Jitao, Chen Lifu, Lin Sen, Ye Chucang, and others also attended and led the ceremony, presenting wreaths and paying respects in the memorial hall before returning to the city. (13th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The speech delivered by Chiang Kai-shek at the opening of the Congress was not fully published in yesterday's newspaper. The following is a continuation:

In the past, our Party not only lacked a spirit of unity but also disrespected discipline. This phenomenon occurred even when the Premier was alive. At that time, many comrades only wanted personal freedom and could not fight for the Party's freedom. They only wanted personal power and could not increase the Party's power. They even opposed the Premier's intentions and insulted the Premier's leadership. Therefore, in his later years, the Premier constantly instructed us to abide by discipline. I remember that the day before the Premier left Guangdong for Beiping in 1924, he told us that he was going to Beijing alone to fight the warlords and hoped that young students and Party members would remember that the most important thing was to "sacrifice personal freedom and contribute each individual's freedom and equality to the revolutionary party. The party's discipline must be observed, and the party's orders must be obeyed. Only the party is allowed to be free; individuals cannot be free. Only then can the revolution succeed." I remember that the Premier also said that the Chinese Nationalist Revolution, from the Tongmenghui to 1924, had not succeeded because everyone agreed today and could form a group, but tomorrow, if their personal interests clashed with the group's interests, they would not hesitate to destroy the group, attack the leader, and scatter the forces to pursue their personal interests. Now, when we think of the Premier's last words, all comrades must feel very pained. Since 1926, the power of all warlords and bureaucrats in the country has been gradually weakened by our Party. After 1928, the Party and the country were completely unified, but unexpectedly, internal disputes within our Party suddenly arose at this time, causing the unification cause to fail just before its completion. By this year, we have reached a state where internal troubles and foreign aggression, natural disasters, and man-made calamities are all pressing down on us simultaneously. Recalling the Premier's words that the revolutionary cause cannot be destroyed by enemies but is destroyed by our own Party, it truly makes us extremely saddened. After each revolutionary failure, the Premier always instructed comrades to examine their own mistakes and find the root cause of the failure. Today, as the Fourth Plenary Session opens here, the Central Committee members feel very ashamed of the past achievements. Even if our comrades across the country do not blame us, how can we forgive ourselves? However, today's internal troubles and foreign aggression, natural disasters, and man-made calamities are truly unprecedented national crises. Not only are the Central Committee members failing in their duties, but even if we combine the talents and efforts of all Party comrades to face the national crisis, we fear that our strength will be insufficient. Therefore, all Party members have a common feeling recently, which is that everyone feels that we must first unite internally and resolve the disputes within our Party before we can resist foreign aggression. As for how to achieve the Party's unity, the prerequisite is naturally mutual love and sincerity, but at the same time, we must not harm the Party's basic organization. Therefore, the comrades attending the Fourth Plenary Session bear a great responsibility. Everyone must, without violating the Party Constitution and the Premier's instructions, use the Congress's common will to study how to unite comrades. If we cannot come up with a truly united method, not only will we be invaded and oppressed by Japan, but the future of the entire Chinese nation will be unimaginably dangerous. This Congress is the Party's highest authority meeting. Everyone must, without betraying the Party's discipline and the Congress's dignity, promote the Party's spiritual unity to jointly resist foreign aggression. In short, the two most important missions of this Congress are (1) to unite internally and (2) to resist foreign aggression. This mission is even more important than the two major missions of reorganizing the Party and transforming China that were carried out when the First National Congress was held. To shoulder this major responsibility, I believe we must pay attention to two things: one is revolutionary morality, and the other is revolutionary spirit. What is revolutionary morality? At a time when the revolution is in danger of failing and the nation's faith in our Party is gradually being lost, and when an unprecedented national crisis is testing our revolutionary morality, we must sacrifice personal freedom, respect the Party's discipline, obey the Congress's common will, and demonstrate the highest morality of a revolutionary party. What is revolutionary spirit? It is what the Premier said: to have the spirit of sacrificing oneself for righteousness, sacrificing everything, including life, for the country and the nation. At this time, we must have the spirit of leading the people to sacrifice themselves for the country in order to save our national destiny. In other words, we must not be negligent or wavering in the slightest. We must devote all our efforts to where righteousness leads us and base everything on the great cause of the revolution. If we can restore this revolutionary morality and revive our revolutionary spirit, then all the work of resisting foreign aggression and uniting internally will surely be realized. If all comrades can regard the Party and the country's interests as their own, I believe that no problem within the Party cannot be resolved, and no differences or right and wrong cannot be resolved with our sincerity. Uniting as one is naturally not a problem, and the Party and the country's future will naturally be bright and consolidated. We unanimously believe that Party unity is our only way out at present, because objective facts cannot but lead us to this conclusion. We propose that past disputes should be resolved with the spirit of solidarity between comrades that the Premier spoke of. As long as it does not violate the Party Constitution and the Premier's instructions, we should make every effort to achieve our unity, no matter what. This does not mean that the Central Committee disregards everything in the past and casually destroys the Party's system. Now, with the national crisis at hand, all our representative comrades must know that (1) Japan's tyrannical aggression is expanding day by day, and (2) after the floods and banditry, the people are already living in misery. Recently, under the double pressure of internal and external troubles, not only the people of the Northeast provinces are suffering greatly, but all compatriots across the country are in extreme hardship. The social economy and the people's livelihood have reached the point of bankruptcy. We should study how to resolve this difficult situation in our Congress. According to the current revolutionary environment, if we want to save the country, the only way is to unite internally; if we want to save the Party, the only way is to unite internally; and if we want to deal with external issues, we must especially unite internally. Revolution requires strategy. With the national crisis at hand, we must study whether it is more important to resolve external issues or internal issues. If we want to be unyielding and uncompromising externally, the only way is to seek unity internally. If we are unwilling to make concessions internally, then we will not be able to make progress externally. Not only will we not be able to make progress, but the effects of dealing with external and internal issues will be completely inversely proportional. I believe that if we can take a step back internally, we can take ten steps forward externally. If we insist on taking a step forward internally, the result will inevitably be a complete failure externally. This is an inevitable law. The representative comrades must be able to examine the environment of our Party and the country and make appropriate decisions. The Premier told us that our Party members must take uniform steps, obey the Party, advance together, and retreat together. The spirit of unity of our revolutionary party lies in advancing and retreating together and sharing life and death. The Party's life and the Party members' lives are one, and the Party's mission is to revolutionize and save the country. We talk about unity and tolerance for the sake of revolutionizing and saving the country. Therefore, we believe that the realization of unity should be promoted by sacrificing everything, but it should not violate the Party Constitution and the Premier's instructions, nor should it violate the public will of the Fourth Plenary Session. Otherwise, if only a part of the goal of unity is achieved while the spirit and discipline of the entire Party are damaged, it will be of no benefit to the Party or the country. In short, I sincerely hope that the representative comrades of the Congress will recognize our environment and facts, and under the premise of protecting the Party's foundation and not betraying the Party's discipline, realize our unity and resist the unprecedented foreign aggression, so as not to let down our Premier and martyrs, and to be worthy of all Party comrades and compatriots across the country. I sincerely wish the Congress success. (13th Dispatch)

Bandit Suppression by Various Armies in Southern Henan Is Smooth

(Nanjing) Bandit suppression by various armies in southern Henan: 1. Bandits have been cleared from Gushi, southeast of about 80 li, from Hekou to Longji, and there are no traces of bandits in the surrounding area; 2. Near Yejiaji, about 100 li east of Shangcheng, 100 bandits burned down a rural village. The bandits suffered heavy casualties after being bombed by the air force; 3. More than 1,000 bandits in Shangrengang, Renliji, and other places about 30 li south of Huangchuan are moving towards Huangchuan, seemingly in an offensive posture, and hundreds of them have been bombed by our air force squadron. (13th Dispatch)

Orders

The National Government ordered on the 13th to appoint Chiang Kai-shek, Lin Sen, Yu Youren, Soong Ziwen, He Yingqin, Li Yuying, Shao Yuanchong, Zhang Xueliang, Xu Yongchang, Han Fuqu, Rong Zongjing, Liu Hongsheng, Fan Xudong, Yu Hede, Zhang Gongquan, Li Fuxun, Wu Daquan, Zhou Zuomin, Gu Mengyu, Hu Shi, Ma Yinchu, Zhu Jiahua, and Yang Quan as members of the Finance Committee, with Chiang Kai-shek as the chairman. This order. Also ordered to appoint Wen Yingsing as the deputy commander of the constabulary. This order. Also ordered to appoint Deng Shizeng as the Chief of Staff of the Garrison Commander's Office of the Nanjing-Shanghai Garrison. This order.

Foreign Important Telegrams

Ex-King Alfonso of Spain Sentenced to Life Imprisonment

Reuters, Madrid, December 12: The so-called Crimes Committee today sentenced former King Alfonso to life imprisonment and confiscated all his property for committing treason. When the committee's report was read in Congress today, the crowd cheered. According to the committee, the reason for not imposing the death penalty was that the new law had abolished the death penalty. However, if Alfonso continues to engage in treasonous activities, he will still be sentenced to death.

An Important Agreement Has Been Reached on the Issue of Ethnic Minorities in India

Reuters, London, December 12: An important agreement determining the demands of ethnic minorities in India in the future constitution was signed today by representatives of Muslims, oppressed classes, Indian Christians, Anglo-Indians, and Europeans. The chief Muslim representative, Aga Khan, is expected to report the agreement to the Minorities Committee of the Round Table Conference tomorrow, at which time he will ask Indian Hindu leaders to accept it. Although the agreement is a significant step forward, the larger issues between Hindus and Muslims in India remain to be resolved.

London Raw Wool Prices Down Three and One Quarter Pence

National News Agency, London, December 13: London raw wool prices closed today. Near term was 21 pence 125, far term was 20 pence 9375, both down three and one quarter pence from yesterday.

Public Telegram

Guangzhou Telegram, To all levels of Party headquarters, representatives of the Fourth National Congress, newspaper offices, and compatriots from all walks of life: This Party's Fourth National Congress, which was previously resolved by this conference to be held on November 12, has been notified accordingly. Subsequently, with the start of peace talks, the date of the Congress was originally scheduled to be jointly decided by the representatives of the peace talks after consulting the central authorities of both sides. Now that the conference period is approaching, the representatives of this conference attending the peace talks are about to return to Guangdong to report. It has been resolved by this conference that the Fourth National Congress will be postponed for a few days and a specific date will be announced later. Specially telegraphed for your information. True Seal of the Extraordinary Meeting of the Central Executive and Supervisory Committees of the Chinese Nationalist Party.

Important News

Black Army Inflicts Heavy Damage on Japanese寇

Anti-Aircraft Guns Shoot Down Enemy Plane, Garrison Troops Shell and Kill Many Japanese Troops

│The First Victorious Battle of Our National Army in the Afternoon of 甲│

Harbin Dispatch: The Japanese army, coercing Zhang Haipeng's rebel forces, launched a large-scale invasion of Heilongjiang. Their intention towards the Black Army was to annihilate them in a single blow, because the Black Army's equipment was outdated and their supplies were inadequate. Compared to the elite troops of Liaoning, they were worlds apart. Therefore, on the 4th, they used heavy troops to pressure Jiangqiao Station, originally hoping to scare away the Black Army without bloodshed, and to cover Zhang Haipeng's entry into Heilongjiang, making him the general they had envisioned. Who would have known that things would turn out so differently? Since the outbreak of hostilities on the 4th, the Japanese army successively increased to two brigades and three regiments, totaling eight to nine thousand men, plus more than seven thousand of Zhang Haipeng's rebel troops, bringing the total force to fifteen or sixteen thousand men, with as many as thirty artillery pieces, and the advantage of more than twenty aircraft. After three days of fierce fighting, they failed to advance even a step beyond Daxing Station, and eventually suffered a defeat and fled in disarray. This was truly an unexpected and unprecedented humiliation for the "Imperial Royal Army." According to military experts, the defeat of the Japanese troops this time was due to the Black Army's extreme courage and determination, with each soldier fighting to the death. However, the arrogance and complacency of the Japanese troops, who did not take our army seriously, was also a cause of their defeat. At a time when the whole country feared Japan like a tiger, the Black Army, under the command of Ma Zhanshan, was able to confront the enemy for several days with a few isolated troops stationed outside the Great Wall, wiping away the great shame of the national army being inferior to the enemy for the past thirty years. This is truly admirable. If all the officers and soldiers in the country were like Ma Zhanshan,

inspired by the bravery of the Black Army, expelling the violent Japanese would not be difficult. The following is an account of the Black Army's heavy defeat of the Japanese寇:

On the 6th, at around 3 p.m., the Japanese troops, besieged by our army, used hand-held machine guns and hand grenades as a vanguard, charging desperately. The aircraft flew very low in the sky, dropping bombs accurately, causing our cavalry line to shift slightly. The Japanese troops then rushed out like wolves and pigs, breaking out of the encirclement and leaving. At around 4 p.m., the Japanese side used two aircraft, taking turns dropping bombs to harass us. Our army did its best to cope until sunset, when the aircraft left, and our army was able to rest. There were no fortifications or villages nearby, making it difficult to supply provisions. Fortunately, the merchants of Ang'angxi and Qiqihar, moved by righteous indignation, made noodles and dry rations, which were transported by cars, and our army was able to fill their stomachs. After 9 p.m., a large force of Japanese troops attacked again. The soldiers fixed bayonets and charged, shouting and killing. Zhang Haipeng's two sons and the commander of the sixth regiment each supervised their troops, encircling from the left and right wings. The terrain was a vast plain, ideal for cavalry. Zhang's Mongol bandits displayed their superb control skills, using one horse and three guns, firing continuously, causing our army considerable trouble. The soldiers fought individually, and those without bayonets on their guns used their gun butts to block and repel the enemy, fighting bravely. Enemy soldiers with broken chests and dragging intestines fell from their horses in heaps. The newly formed garrison army brigade was particularly experienced in combat, firing mortars fiercely, scattering the enemy's dense formations. The enemy lost coordination, and our army took advantage of the situation to sweep with infantry machine guns, causing the enemy to retreat slightly and switch to artillery bombardment. Our garrison army was originally reorganized from the famous artillery brigade of the Northeast, and their aim was very accurate. They fired mountain guns and anti-aircraft guns in direct fire, hitting the target accurately, and the enemy also suffered considerable losses. By 1 a.m. on the 7th, the artillery bombardment gradually subsided, and our army also ceased firing back. At this time, Zhang Dianjiu's troops of the Black Army rushed from Zhalantun, increasing their strength and boosting morale. After 5 a.m., the Japanese army launched a dawn attack, using cavalry to detour to Daxingtun and Xiaoxintun, to take our rear. Our army took the opportunity to feign a retreat of twenty li, pre-positioning artillery at Sanjianfang and Huluxi Station. The Japanese army and Zhang's rebel troops did not realize this and bravely pursued. Our artillery then took advantage of the high ground to launch a fierce bombardment. It is said that this battle killed more than 600 Japanese soldiers, and the death toll among Zhang's rebel troops was even higher, at more than a thousand. Nine Japanese aircraft came to support, circling overhead and dropping bombs. They flew extremely low, and the garrison troops set up anti-aircraft guns in direct fire, firing into the air, and shot down one of the aircraft. The other aircraft, thinking that our army had anti-aircraft guns, did not dare to linger and flew away. With the Japanese army losing support, our army was able to calmly counterattack. By about 10 a.m., the Japanese army and Zhang's rebel troops had suffered more and more casualties, and dared not continue fighting, retreating in disarray to the left of Jiangqiao, fleeing about fifty li, with corpses strewn across the field and countless supplies abandoned. Our army then pursued to Jiangqiao Station, still firmly defending the original defense. The fighting stopped at noon. Black Chairman Ma Zhanshan rushed from the provincial capital to the front to comfort the troops, encourage the soldiers, and comfort the wounded. He also designated the area from Jiangqiao Station in the south to Xinlitun and in the north to Daguantun as the first line of defense, defended by Wu Songshan's brigade with two regiments of garrison troops. Daxing Station, Sijiazi, and Sanjianfang were designated as the second line of defense, defended by two infantry regiments of Zhang Dianjiu's troops and one infantry regiment of garrison troops. Xiaoxintun and Huluxi were designated as the third line of defense, and two regiments of Su Bingwen's brigade and one cavalry regiment of Cheng Zhiyuan's brigade have been transferred to defend it. The defenses are extremely tight and the communication is appropriate. Example Diagram: "Our Army's Defense Line After the Battle"

to prepare for the enemy's return. The Black Province's combat-ready troops have now been mostly transferred to the front, and the defenses along the Eastern Railway's Harbin-Manchuria line are inevitably empty. Ma Zhanshan specially obtained Ding Chao's agreement to transfer the 661st Regiment of the 22nd Brigade of the Jilin Army under Su Dechen from the Harbin-Changchun line, and the 2nd and 3rd battalions of infantry to Ang'angxi Station, and the 1st Battalion of the 674th Regiment of the 26th Brigade of Xing Zhanqing to Zhalantun Station, and the 1st Battalion of the 679th Regiment of the 28th Brigade of Ding Chao to Fularji Station, to replace the Black Army in protecting the railway. Currently, the people of Harbin are overjoyed by the Black Army's defeat of the violent Japanese寇this time, and have launched a campaign to comfort the troops, collecting funds to purchase goods to send to the front to comfort them. (7th)

Panic in Tianjin Not Abated

Tianjin Dispatch: This reporter went to Zhang Mayor Xueming's private residence on No. 17 Road in the Special Area No. 1 on the afternoon of the 10th to interview him. It was then learned that the provincial and municipal authorities were all working in Hebei, so he drove straight to Hebei. The following is a draft of this dispatch based on the information obtained from the interview.

Visiting the Municipal Public Security Bureau, the reporter passed through British Central Street in the Special Area No. 1, and there was nothing unusual, except that there were fewer pedestrians and vehicles. Passing through Central Street in the French Concession, four tanks were glimpsed parked in front of the French Army Headquarters. Entering the Special Area No. 3 through the Wanguo Bridge, there were double guards everywhere, and the pedestrians were as sparse as the morning stars, and looking around, their faces showed panic. Entering the Italian Concession, the intersections connecting the east with Special Area No. 3, the intersections connecting the west with Special Area No. 2, and the area along the river in the south, were all piled with earthbags, set up with electric nets and machine guns, and guarded by foreign sailors with guns. These sailors wore green uniforms and steel helmets. The Public Security Bureau is directly across the river from Special Area No. 2. Japanese soldiers and plainclothes agents fired at the Public Security Bureau day and night. Many stray bullets fell into Special Area No. 2. Although there were no casualties among the residents, many glass doors and windows were broken, and every household was closed, resembling a New Year's scene. Both ends of the Dongfu Bridge and in front of the Public Security Bureau were piled with sandbags, each guarded by more than a dozen members of the security team with guns. Entering the Public Security Bureau, the inspection was very strict. It happened that Wu Yixian, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau (and Secretary-General of the Public Security Bureau), was working inside. According to Wu, the mayor came to the bureau this afternoon to interrogate the plainclothes agents, and one of them had been executed and his head displayed to the public. There are still more than 100 Northeastern refugee students in the Caojia Building in Special Area No. 2 who have not found suitable schools. Due to the curfew, they have been without food for two days. I have just issued them 50 yuan to temporarily maintain their lives. The Japanese in the Yuda Cotton Mill, a Japanese business in Xiaoliuzhuang, Special Area No. 1, have fled into the Japanese Concession last night. The factory has suspended work today, and more than 3,000 workers have immediately lost their jobs. In this time of terror, adding this hidden worry, there is no way to provide relief for the time being. On the morning of the 9th, Japanese soldiers bombarded the Public Security Bureau with mountain guns. It has now been ascertained that one shell landed on the top floor of the Engineering Department of the Second Telephone Bureau, destroying the roof. One shell landed in the Tonghecheng Dye Shop on Yanghuo Street, destroying the awning. One shell also landed in front of the Public Security Bureau, but did not explode. It was one foot long, with a circumference diameter of four inches, and had the words "Made in the 5th Year of Taisho" on it. According to the report of the security police who were guarding at the time, there were also three artillery shells that landed in the river by the Dongfu Bridge, and people are being hired to salvage them, but they have not yet been retrieved. Also recovered were bullets fired from the Japanese Concession, with the words "Made by Han Linchun" on them. This type of bullet was manufactured by the Three Eastern Provinces Arsenal in the 11th year of the Republic of China, and was stored in the warehouse unused. Now it has suddenly been discovered in this incident. This proves that after the Japanese army occupied Shenyang, they transported the guns and ammunition from the Three Eastern Provinces Arsenal to Lushun. Because in the late last month, a Japanese merchant ship (the date and name of the ship are no longer remembered) sailed from Lushun, loaded with more than seventy boxes of munitions on the 4th. After arriving in Tianjin, it was unloaded into the Japanese barracks. On the 5th of this month, the Japanese ship Tenchomaru also loaded more than three hundred boxes of munitions from Lushun and unloaded them into the Japanese barracks in Tanggu. At that time, the Japanese side used the excuse of military supplies to refuse customs inspection. Although the Japanese authorities have repeatedly denied secretly assisting the plainclothes agents, the artillery shells and bullets are conclusive evidence, and the facts are the most eloquent. I am afraid that it will be impossible to conceal them in the end. After Wu finished talking, he hurried away from the bureau. Suddenly, several gunshots were heard, originating from the gate of the Japanese Concession. The bullets flew through the air with a whooshing sound. The reporter felt that he could not stay for long, so he got into the car and went through Shuige Street, turning into Dongma Road. In the Dahu District of the Guanyinhao area, where vehicles and horses were usually noisy and carriages were connected, the merchants were now tightly closed and no pedestrians were seen. Entering the provincial government through the Jingang Bridge, he was inspected five or six times along the way.

Visiting the Provincial and Municipal Governments, the reporter entered the provincial government and submitted his card to the transmission office to request an audience with Chairman Wang Shuchang. He was received and, according to Wang, the riot by the plainclothes agents was planned and organized. If they did not rely on the secret assistance of foreigners in the concession, where would they get so many guns and bullets? Although local order has been disrupted by these people, fortunately, the police and security forces have been able to cope calmly, loyally and dutifully. As a provincial official, I have the responsibility to defend the territory and will never be intimidated. Commander-in-Chief Jiang sends telegrams every day to inquire about the situation, instructing me and Mayor Zhang to defend strictly. Deputy Commander Zhang also gives instructions on the situation by long-distance telephone from time to time. The plainclothes agents rely on the secret assistance of a certain country and their actions are erratic, but they are an undisciplined rabble and have not received military training. If they do not rely on the protection of the concession, even if there were three or five thousand more of them, they would be easily suppressed. The reporter took his leave and went to the municipal government again, but heard that Mayor Zhang had not arrived and only Liu Bangban was working inside. He then went to the Beining Railway Bureau to visit Director Gao Jiyi. He learned that the Japanese destroyer Karukaya of the Lushun-based Japanese destroyer fleet, carrying more than 300 marines, had arrived in Tanggu at 1 p.m. today (the 10th). Because the Haihe River is shallow, they will sail to Tianjin when the tide rises tonight. He then went to the New Railway Station for inspection and saw soldiers of the 6th Company of the 2nd Battalion of the 654th Regiment of the 15th Brigade of the Northeast, responsible for station security. The tracks and bridges from the Old Station in the east to Beicang in the north were all patrolled by soldiers of that company. A row of Northeastern armored vehicles was parked on the platform, led by Captain Zhao Liangbi with more than 300 soldiers, responsible for the road protection mission between Pingjin. Rumors were rife in the Hebei area, spreading that Japanese soldiers were scheduled to assist the plainclothes agents in a general attack on the Public Security Bureau and the provincial and municipal governments tonight (the 10th). The area had already been placed under martial law at 5 p.m. in advance, cutting off traffic. The personnel of the Beining Railway Bureau and the Tianjin Office of the Jinpu Railway also left work early at 4 p.m. The reporter, fearing that traffic would be cut off, dared not stay for long. On the way back, he turned to the Municipal Party Department for a look, but the staff had all left. He then got into the car and, after several inspections, entered the Wanguo Bridge. Passing by Lizhan, he saw four trucks carrying armed Japanese soldiers, about fifty or sixty of them, driving towards the French Concession. The reporter hurriedly ordered the driver to follow closely behind to see what was going on. However, the car drove extremely fast and disappeared after reaching the British Concession. He then returned home dejectedly. He then used the telephone to inquire in all directions, and only then did he learn that the Japanese soldiers had gone to the Dalian Pier in Special Area No. 1 to board small motorboats and sailed downstream. It can be inferred that they must have been ordered by Japanese Commander Kashi to go to Tanggu to convey important matters to the Karukaya. Since the night of the incident, long-distance calls, except for the provincial and municipal government agencies, have all been suspended. The Japanese army also included the telephone to Tanggu in the suspension list.

The Disturbances of the Night of the 10th. Yesterday, rumors spread that Japanese soldiers were scheduled to assist the plainclothes agents in launching a general attack at 12 p.m. For the sake of preventing any eventuality, the provincial and municipal authorities ordered a special curfew and issued two hand grenades to the police in Special Areas 1, 2, and 3. At around 8 p.m., the Wanguo Bridge was pulled open, cutting off traffic. At night, dozens of Japanese soldiers took four small motorboats to patrol the Haihe River to demonstrate. After 9 p.m., gunshots were heard intermittently. At 11 p.m., the gunshots became tighter. At 12 p.m., the gunshots became even more intense, as dense as broken beads. This morning (the 11th), at 2 a.m., the sound of artillery boomed, still from the Japanese barracks in Haiguang Temple and the gate of the Japanese Concession. By 6 a.m., there were about twenty explosions in total. This afternoon, inquiring in all directions, it was learned that three or forty plainclothes agents were discovered inside Ximen at 11 p.m. last night and were dispersed by the police. In other places, such as Nankai Guangdeli, Yanghuqiao, Nantou Guantou, and Nanshi, groups of thirty to fifty plainclothes agents were discovered and were all routed by the security forces, and more than a dozen were captured. The plainclothes agents surrounded in Paotaizhuang Wandezhuang were suddenly relieved by dozens of Japanese soldiers this morning, who took the plainclothes agents into the Japanese Concession. The Sixth Sub-Bureau in the Second District has been guarded by Japanese military police. The municipal government is scheduled to protest to the Japanese consul this afternoon, demanding that the Japanese military police withdraw immediately. The Public Security Bureau, in response to the request of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, has allowed merchants and residents to go out to purchase food under police supervision and protection from 10 a.m. to 1 p.m. Japanese Commander issued an order this morning that all Japanese women and children evacuate into the Japanese barracks, and all Japanese men went to the Veterans Association to await dispatch. Gunshots continue throughout the day today. Chinese territory will cut off traffic after 2 p.m. this afternoon, and the situation is still extremely dangerous. (Afternoon of the 11th)

Serious Situation in Wuhan

Nine Japanese Warships Arrive, Hull to Hull, The Garrison Command Has Advanced the Curfew Time

Hankou Dispatch: After the Japanese troops forcibly occupied Liaoning and Jilin, they again attacked Heilongjiang and disturbed Tianjin. The situation is becoming increasingly serious. Recently, the Yangtze River has also continued to increase troops, and the situation in the corner of Wuhan is particularly serious. Director He Chengjun of the Military Affairs Commission originally planned to go to Beijing to attend the Fourth Plenary Session, but was temporarily ordered by Commander-in-Chief Jiang to sit in Wuhan and has ceased to travel. At first, the Japanese sent warships to Wuhan one after another in the name of protecting overseas Chinese, including Hirado, Hira, Urakaze, No. 24, Hoz, and Kotaka, a total of six ships. Later, the Hoz, No. 24, and Hira were ordered to be transferred elsewhere and replaced by Hinoki, Hairokku, and Sumida. By 10 a.m. on the 9th, the 10,000-ton flagship Atago and two destroyers, Momokashi, also arrived in Hankou. Including the previous ships, there are a total of nine ships. Atago, Hirado, Sumida, Hairokku, Kotaka, Kashi, Momo, Hinoki, etc. were eight ships parked in the Japanese Concession Jiang surface. One Urakaze was moored along the river at the Six Pier of the Special Area No. 2. The hulls were connected to each other, the defenses were heavily guarded, and I really don’t know what their intentions are. Atago stationed Japanese Navy Commander Shiozawa, and all ships are under his command. After arriving in Hankou, he held secret meetings in the Japanese Concession with the captains of each ship and the consuls in Hankou, Chongqing, Chengdu and Zhengzhou. Overseas Japanese and vagrant people also seem to be receiving his hints, constantly provoking trouble. According to a certain source, the overseas Japanese recently received instructions from the Japanese government to arm themselves and seize opportunities to launch incidents, corroborating the previous rumors that the Japanese would riot in Tianjin, Shanghai, Guangzhou and Hankou. It is not without reason. The people of Wuhan are extremely indignant at this violent invasion. However, upholding the government's intention to strive for peace and calm struggle, they are doing their best to avoid conflict. No matter how the Japanese provoke, they tolerate it as much as possible. Therefore, no accident has occurred. It is heard that the authorities recently held discussions, on the one hand, to do their best to protect the overseas Japanese, and on the other hand, to order the people to endure humiliation and bear burdens, so that the Japanese will never find an excuse. At the same time, the Garrison Command also issued a notice, starting from the 10th of this month, advancing the curfew time, cutting off traffic every night at 10 p.m. to avoid the mingling of petty criminals. As for the anti-Japanese movement, it is becoming increasingly tense due to the Japanese violence. The registration of Japanese goods by the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association ended on the 10th and the general inspection began. At 7 p.m. on the 10th, the association held an emergency meeting to discuss inspection methods and precautions for inspectors to avoid the Japanese provoking trouble, and invited the business community's trade associations to organize inspection teams to assist in the process. The measures have been drafted and a letter has been sent to each trade association for verification. (November 10)

Local Correspondence

Suzhou

The water police have suppressed bandits and rescued hostages. The Su-Xi water police rescued two persons, Yan Jisheng, who had been kidnapped on Maji Mountain, Taihu Lake. Yesterday, they rescued four persons: Ge Shi, Zhu Lisheng, Li Ahong, and Jin Aquan. All were kidnap victims from the Fei Yun Wheel. They were immediately sent back to Dongshan.

Wuxi

The Wuxi Flood Relief and Reconstruction Association held its eighth cadre board meeting yesterday to discuss the approval of the provincial government to transfer the land tax for road construction to repair dike projects, and also County Chief Chen and Construction Bureau Chief Yao reported that the provincial department continued to send people to Wuxi to guard and collect the land tax for road construction. It was resolved that the local repair of dikes and relief works should be handled by the government. If the province can be responsible, as long as it does not deviate too much from the local plan, the funds raised locally may be handed over to the county and sent to the province for official management. If the provincial department cannot take care of it, then the local government, in view of the imminent disaster in Jiangbei, must take measures for itself. Even if the requested 50,000 yuan of land tax for road construction is transferred in full, it will still be far from enough. Before the provincial department has a definite plan for this case, Hua Yi’s Chen Zhanru should be contacted with Wuxi Jiaotong Bank, and the road construction donation stored in the Construction Bureau shall not be used without the notification of the association.

The League of Nations investigation team visits educational institutions. The Education Investigation Team of the League of Nations, Baker (German), Lanzhiman (French), and four others, came to Wuxi from Shanghai the day before yesterday and stayed at the Meiyuan Taihu Hotel. That evening, the county government, the county party headquarters, and seven other groups held a public banquet at the county chamber of commerce. Yesterday morning, they visited the Shenxin and other textile factories, and the Minfeng and other silk factories. In the afternoon, they visited the Mass Education Institute and the Huangxiang Experimental Area and the Engineering Education Area. After the visit, a Western-style banquet was held at the Mass Education Institute. Today (14th) morning, they will visit the provincial Wuxi Middle School and other primary and secondary schools, and in the afternoon, they will visit the social education institutions and the achievement exhibition.

Zhenjiang

Suiyuan requested to transport grain. The Jiangsu Provincial Relief Association approved the letter from the Suiyuan Provincial Farmers Association, which roughly stated that the floods in Hubei, Anhui, Jiangsu, and Henan this year were a disaster to witness. The province’s harvest is still abundant, and transportation is convenient. We specially request your association to come to our province to collect and transport relief grain to alleviate the people’s food shortage. Our association is willing to do our best to help and provide you with the needs at a low price. Please consider and decide. It has been approved by the provincial relief association and consulted with the disaster-stricken counties in the province to follow suit and transport grain to regulate the food supply in the disaster areas for universal relief.

Hangzhou

A large number of bandits are sentenced separately. The Hangzhou County Public Security Bureau arrested Cai Zilin, Hua Shunsheng, Lu A’da, Yang A’gen, and other pirates who robbed ships in Pingyao and sent them to the court. After interrogation, they confessed to robbing in various villages. The trial has concluded, and the sentence was pronounced yesterday. Hua Shunsheng and others were sentenced to 12 years of imprisonment for carrying dangerous weapons and robbery in groups of three or more. Cai Zilin and Yang A’gen were each sentenced to six years of imprisonment for one count of robbery. Lu A’da was sentenced to three years of imprisonment for receiving stolen goods.

Shaoxing

A robbery and injury case occurred in the urban area. The Hengyu Qianzhuang in Xincheng Alley, Shaocheng, is located in a remote area. On the evening of the 11th, two robbers suddenly came. One guarded the door, and one robber entered to rob. Because he did not know where the silver was hidden, he forced him to point out where the silver room was. The clerk of the zhuang knew that they were bandits and replied that he did not know. The bandit immediately took out a sharp knife and stabbed the clerk in the head and fled. The police and military agencies were immediately notified and sent teams to arrest them, but it was too late.
