Gun Burned

The Truth of a Murder for Inheritance is Not Successfully Hidden by Crackling in the Kitchen

Zhang Guoxiang, Zhang Yuxiang, and Zhang Qingxiang, sons of Zhang Linsheng of Huayuan Shiqiao, Pudong, were dividing the inheritance when Yuxiang was shot dead and Guoxiang was seriously injured. After investigation by the Third District Police Station, it was found that Zhang Qingxiang was born to Zhang Linsheng's concubine, Zhang Zhang. Zhang Zhang's younger brother, Zhang Quansheng, shot and killed Yuxiang. They were both transferred to the District Court. It is now known that Shen Zhaoming, the prosecutor of the District Court, meticulously investigated the case and determined that Zhang Quansheng was the murderer. He wanted his sister and nephew to inherit the family property alone, so he killed the son of the legal wife. He had a gun for the murder, but it was big and useless, so he exchanged it for a small four-inch pistol from Yang Fulin. His premeditated murder is evident. However, because he was lying in court, he sent Judicial Police Chief Xu Jinqing, along with bailiffs Wang Jianqing and Zhou Qiwu, to search for the gun to use as evidence the day before yesterday. Unexpectedly, after the incident, Zhang Quansheng hid the gun in the stove and burned it, hoping to destroy the evidence temporarily. After being arrested, his wife did not know that there were still bullets in the gun and did not take them out, so she still cooked rice. Unexpectedly, after the fire caught the bullets, there was a sudden crackling in the stove, and the neighbors were terrified, suspecting that it was robbery and blocking the front and back doors to arrest the bandits. Zhang's wife, in a hurry, hid the gun again and buried it in the field afterward. Therefore, when Police Chief Xu and others went to search, they could not find it at the time. After using detective methods to find out the previous situation, they first found two exploded bullets in the stove. Then, they used various methods and words to force Zhang's wife to lead them to the field to find the gun, but it had already been burned. They brought the gun and bullets to the court and reported the situation to Prosecutor Shen. Since the facts of the case are evident, he ordered them to be stored in the warehouse together, awaiting strict handling according to the law.

How Can the Dignity of the Court Allow Abuse and Protection?

Dong Zhenlong's Careless Words Make Zhang Baofeng Feel Unhappy, and He Files a Lawsuit for Public Insult

Dong Zhenlong, the manager of the Shenzhou Hotel on Fourth Avenue, was involved in a lawsuit with others over a housing dispute on the afternoon of October 23 of this year in the First Court of the Special District. At that time, there was a Ningbo native named Zhang Baofeng

Page 12

, who used to be a tenant of the Shenzhou Hotel's property. He was also one of the parties involved in the case, so he was summoned to court for the trial. When the judge was questioning him, Dong said that Zhang's testimony was contrary to his intentions and publicly abused him as "fang bi". After the adjournment, he scolded him as a "robber" in front of the seventh court. Therefore, Zhang Baofeng yesterday commissioned Lawyer Gu Jirong to accuse him of the crime of publicly insulting and defaming his reputation in accordance with Article 324 of the Criminal Law in the First Court of the Special District. Judge Feng heard the case in the second criminal court. First, the plaintiff stated as above and pointed out that there were two witnesses, Shan Xingwu and Chen Daosheng, who had heard the abuse. Judge Feng then summoned Shan Xingwu to testify. Shan said that he did not know Zhang and Dong personally. At that time, he was in the court to listen to another case. After Dong scolded Zhang, the audience in the court was in an uproar, thinking that the court was a place of dignity and it was strange to publicly scold people. After leaving the court, Zhang blamed Dong for not scolding him as "fang bi". Dong also scolded him as "You are simply a robber!" At that time, Zhang immediately asked me for my position and asked me to be a witness, so I came to court today to testify. Then, Dong Zhenlong was questioned. He said that in the court, in his reply to Judge Lu, because what Zhang said was inconsistent with the facts of the case, he used the meaning of analogy to say that his words were like "fang bi" and did not scold him personally. Then Zhang continued to say that the "fang bi" he said to Judge Lu did not refer to him, then it must refer to Judge Lu. If that is the case, then he is willing to have Judge Lu sue him, and it has nothing to do with him, because if he does not refer to him, then he must refer to the judge. At this point, the defendant also stated that the plaintiff deliberately slandered and insulted his reputation, and that when the case was not yet public, the Shibao had already published the plaintiff's complaint, which shows that he deliberately publicized it to damage his personal reputation. He presented the newspaper to the court. After Judge Feng read it, he asked Lawyer Gu, "This case has not been publicly tried. How could the reporter of the newspaper record the complaint?" Lawyer Gu replied, "Our reporters often come in and out, and I don't know how they recorded it. However, newspaper reporters have extremely flexible means of obtaining news, which has been recognized by the society, so I don't know how they got it. However, our lawyer personally has absolutely not given the complaint of this case to the reporter." At this point, the court ordered the debate to begin. After the lawyers of both sides debated, the court announced that the sentence would be pronounced on the afternoon of the 18th.

Shareholders of Zhihe Money Shop Accused

Should Be Liable for Jointly Repaying the Debt

Zhihe Yongji Money Shop went bankrupt on August 19, owing a huge debt of 2.5 million taels. The debt claims also amounted to 2.5 million taels, of which many were bad debts. For example, Shen Chengji's account owed 1.2 million taels, and the person himself has already fled, making it impossible to recover. Many shareholders are also avoiding appearing. The court-appointed liquidator, Accountant Tang Zaizhang, is legally carrying out liquidation. In addition to collecting debt claims to prepare for an average repayment of debts, he also found the shareholders' register and sent letters to the shareholders asking them to come forward to deal with the matter. Because many shareholders made excuses and shirked responsibility, he specifically filed a lawsuit with the court, asking the court to order the partners to be jointly and severally liable for repayment. The court opened the case in the First Special District District Court yesterday. Many creditors attended the court to listen. The presiding judge was Judge Li Mo, the plaintiff was Accountant Tang Zaizhang, and the lawyers representing the plaintiff were Wang Youling. The lawyers representing the defendant shareholders Chen Yizhai were Wu Jingxiong and Wang Fusang, and the lawyer representing shareholder Chen Rongchu was Zhang Zhengxue. The remaining shareholders did not appear in court. After reviewing the various accounts, the court scheduled another hearing for debate on the 24th of this month.

Hu Fufang Killed by Kidnappers

A Coroner's Examination

The Negotiations Were Not Very Smooth and the Corpse Was Collected by His Younger Brother for Burial

The Shanghai police officer No. 873 of the Jing'an Temple Police Station found a white package abandoned opposite the house No. 14 of Southwest Yang Road in Shanghai the night before last. There were blood stains on the outside. He opened the package and found a dismembered body inside. The hands, feet, and head had been cut off. He reported to the police station and ordered the detectives to transport the body to the Feilun Road Mortuary for examination. Details have been recorded in this newspaper. It is now known that the name of the dismembered body is Hu Fufang, 34 years old, a native of Shanghai, living at No. 811 Weihaiwei Road, operating a rice shop. His family is well-off. He also purchased land on Tongfu Road to build three houses, which are about to be completed. On the 17th of last month, Hu went to visit the new house and was kidnapped by several kidnappers at the intersection of Tongfu Road and Weihaiwei Road. They immediately sent a letter to his family, demanding a huge ransom. For more than half a month, the negotiations were not very smooth, and the kidnappers resented Hu and killed him. Then they dismembered the body and abandoned it on the side of the road. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, the prosecutor of the First Special District Court, accompanied the forensic doctor Wei Ligong and the clerk Liu Chun to the mortuary for examination. The examination confirmed that Hu's body was at the public's disposal. First, the police station stated the facts of the discovery of the body and Hu's kidnapping. Then Hu Jinfang, the younger brother of the deceased, came to the case and requested to collect the body. Prosecutor Guo verified and ordered that Hu Fufang was indeed strangled to death by bandits and then dismembered. The body was returned to his younger brother Hu Jinfang for coffin burial, and the police station was ordered to strictly arrest the murderers and bring them to justice.

Five Policemen Injured by a Car

Lu Peiwang, a native of Yangzhou, living at No. 36 Hanzhong Lane, Hanzhong Road, Zhabei, was a driver for Sichuan Automobile Company on Avenue Joffre. On the evening of the 3rd of this month, he drove a car No. 12609 and drove to Avenue Lafayette at 12 o'clock, from west to east. There were nine Chinese police officers from the French Concession Police Station walking in front of him. The driver Lu accidentally knocked down five police officers, No. 256 Xu Zhengrong, No. 235 Cao Asi, No. 612 Chen Jinrong, No. 666 Lu Hongfu, and No. 697 Tao Benxiang. Their arms, legs, waists, backs, and other parts were injured. The accompanying police officers recorded the number and reported it to the police chief. The injured police officers went to the hospital for treatment. The injuries were minor, and they still went to work as usual. Yesterday, the Vehicle Management Office transferred Lu to the Second District Court Criminal Simple Court. The police station lawyer stated the case and filed a lawsuit in accordance with Article 301 of the Criminal Law. The injured police officers went to court to prove the situation of being hit. When questioned, Lu stated that the police officers were walking in the middle of the road, and the people were unable to brake in time, resulting in the accident. Judge Wu Fanglian verified the confession and ordered the police officers to go to the forensic doctor's office to examine the injuries. He also announced the end of the debate and ordered the defendant to pay 50 yuan and a guarantee. Without a guarantee, he would be detained.

Tragic Abortion Death

Wang Chen's Death is Pitiful, and Dagouzi is the Culprit

Wang Chen, a woman from Yancheng, Jiangbei, is 38 years old and currently lives at No. 1213 Lincoln Road, Shanghai West. Although old, she is unusually flirtatious. Because her husband, Wang, is in the countryside and she is not used to sleeping alone, she suddenly became acquainted with a fellow villager, nicknamed Dagouzi, this spring and lived together as if they were husband and wife. Unexpectedly, after a short time, she suddenly became pregnant and was already several months along. Her abdomen was bulging, and she was afraid that acquaintances would catch a glimpse and spread it to her husband's ears, which was a serious matter. So, four days ago, she entrusted a fellow villager, Xing Cui, to introduce her to Li Lin, who lives at No. 69 Guangfu Road, Caogadu, Shanghai West, to perform an abortion. She stated that the surgery fee was a certain amount of money. Li Lin took out a root of herb and inserted it into Wang Chen's lower body, saying that the fetus would fall out after two hours without worry. Unexpectedly, after three hours, not only did she not give birth, but Wang Chen became extremely painful and fainted, losing consciousness. Seeing that something had gone wrong, Li Lin still said that it was okay and massaged her abdomen with both hands, but it still didn't work. The situation was even more serious, and her limbs were icy cold and dying. She was rushed to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but it was too late to save her. She died in the afternoon of the day before yesterday.

Chen Longhai's Wife Gives Birth to Triplets

Chen Longhai, a native of Jiangyin who lives at No. 12 Minzhu Street, Lao Beimen, and works in copper and tin, is over forty years old and still has the worries of Bodao. He has been married to his wife, Zhang, for ten years and has not had any children. Unexpectedly, she suddenly became pregnant in May of this year. Chen was overjoyed and took great care of her, expecting her to give birth in February next year. Unexpectedly, recently Zhang's abdomen was as big as a bucket. Chen suspected it was a disease and sought medical attention, but it did not worsen. Unexpectedly, in the middle of the night the night before last, Zhang had severe abdominal pain, as if she was about to give birth. Chen quickly hired a midwife to wait for the birth. It was not until yesterday morning that she gave birth to a boy, but the parturient's abdomen was still cramping. Soon, she gave birth to another boy. Who knew that her abdomen was still painful, and she continued to give birth to another boy before stopping. She had a total of three boys in one birth, and they were all plump. The parturient and the children were safe. The neighbors came to see them when they heard the news. They all said that the children who were not yet full-term were so strong, which was indeed rare. Chen named them Xinde, Wangde, and Aide and filled out the forms to report to the First Branch of the Second District.

Change in Business Hours of Postal Branches

The Shanghai Postal Administration, in view of the concentration of commercial firms in the Nanshi and French Concession Central District, will extend the receiving hours of the Gongguan Road, Nanshi Lima Road, and Bund branches to 9:00 PM starting from the 16th of this month for the convenience of senders posting express mail. Also, because the Caogadu branch and the Bairinan Road branch of Wujiaochang are very close, most senders tend to go to the Bairinan Road branch. Starting from the 16th of this month, the business hours of the Caogadu branch will be changed to be from 8:00 AM to 6:00 PM.

Death of Yarn Merchant Xu Qingyun

Yarn merchant Xu Qingyun had been suffering from stomach disease for a long time. Recently, he underwent surgery, but it was not effective. He died at 10:30 AM on the 11th of this month. Mr. Xu was a native of Cixi, Zhejiang, named Pinwei, also named Weixun, styled Qingyun, and was 51 years old. His ancestors in Shanghai had been in the yarn business. After his death, the business was unfavorable, and his assets were exhausted. Mr. Xu was only ten years old at the time. Seeing his mother depressed, he comforted her, saying, "There is still a son. Don't be too sad." So, he vowed to restore his ancestors' business. At the age of sixteen, he came to Shanghai to learn business, worked diligently and thriftily, and was determined to be successful. Within a few years, he had accumulated some surplus. He founded Futai Yarn Shop. At that time, a Western merchant abandoned a large batch of yarn goods in Shanghai due to poor business and returned to his country, which implicated a major bank. Mr. Xu invested heavily to purchase it from him. His peers secretly laughed at him, but he ignored them. Later, he relied on this to make a profit. From then on, Mr. Xu's courage was admired by his peers. When the stock exchange flourished, he and yarn merchants Mu Ouchu, Wu Linshu, Rong Zongjing, and others initiated the organization of the Chinese Yarn Exchange and served as directors and vice-chairmen of the exchange. In the tenth year of the Republic of China, the former Dafeng Yarn Factory closed down. At that time, after the European War, all the yarn factories in the country were greatly affected and suffered huge losses. Therefore, no one bought the former Dafeng Yarn Factory. It was about to be sold to foreign merchants, and the foreign merchants knew that the Chinese merchants did not dare to operate it, so they deliberately made things difficult, hoping to get it at a low price. Mr. Xu said with great emotion, "Can our country's yarn industry be ruined by this? I don't believe it. Moreover, if this factory falls into the hands of foreigners, then foreign merchants will inevitably have one more foundation to monopolize our country's yarn industry." At that time, his close friend Mr. Qin Runqing advised him to buy it, and Mr. Xu made up his mind. So, he bought it at a high price and collected shares to reorganize it, which is now the Shanghai Dafeng Qingji Yarn Factory. Mr. Xu served as chairman and general manager, planning everything in detail. Within a few years, great achievements were made. He also used his surplus funds to invest in banking and other industries with friends. After the May 30th Massacre, the Shanghai money market was extremely tight, and the financial community was worried. Mr. Xu believed that Shanghai was the commercial hub of the country. If there was a crisis in the financial community, it would inevitably affect the whole country. Therefore, he generously invested heavily to maintain it. Also, Mr. Xu lived frugally but was extremely filial to his mother, kind-hearted, and charitable. He made every effort to support social welfare and hometown charity. He served as a director of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and a member of the Labor-Capital Mediation Committee, being selfless and offering many suggestions. Mr. Xu was elected as the captain of the solicitation meeting and raised more than 50,000 yuan in a month. In addition, he served as a director of various charitable organizations, handled rice sales and construction of model prisons in Ningbo, donated to floods in various provinces, and so on, which are too numerous to mention. In the spring of this year, his stomach disease relapsed, and he went to Hangzhou for recuperation. Then he returned to Shanghai. After being treated by Chinese and Western medicine, none of them worked. He died the day before yesterday, which was a pity for those who knew him. It is said that the coffin will be encoffined at the end of the day on the 14th of this month.

Patriotic compatriots should pay attention to it.

Shantytown Residents on Haig Road Appeal to Party and Government Agencies

More than a dozen representatives of the shantytown residents on Haig Road in Shanghai West submitted a request to the Party and government authorities yesterday for assistance. Their submissions to the Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Social Bureau are as follows: Submitted for being ordered to be evicted by the French Concession Police Station, requesting assistance, and praying to be submitted to the Municipal Government to quickly build civilian houses to benefit the people's residences. The residents built shacks and lived along the eastern section of Haig Road in Shanghai West, near Laborier Road, for more than ten years. There are about 200 shacks, with more than a thousand men, women, old, and young. On the 6th of this month, the Police Station of Shan Zhong Road in the French Concession suddenly sent several detectives to come and claim that they were ordered to move out completely within two weeks and demolish the shacks, and not to live in the territory, otherwise they would send people to demolish them. The residents were shocked to hear this. The residents have always been rickshaw pullers, small cart pullers, coolie workers, and small businesses, living peacefully and never acting out of line. Moreover, due to the years of natural disasters and banditry in Jiangbei, they have no way to settle down. Especially this year's floods, they have been groaning to make a living. If they are evicted, the residents will inevitably be displaced, no different from being driven into hell. In addition, the weather is getting colder, and their suffering will be even more difficult to predict. Therefore, they specifically submit a request to your Association (Bureau) to show compassion for their poverty and allow them to submit it to the Municipal Government to quickly build civilian houses in the Shanghai West area so that the residents can move in to live. They also pray that the French Concession Police Station be restrained from interfering with the residents' living problems in Shanghai West before the civilian houses are built. For this reason, they should submit a document to your Association (Bureau), praying for examination and approval, so as to benefit the people's residences, and they will be grateful. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Special Municipality Party Department (Municipal Social Bureau), Haig Road Shantytown Residents Representatives Qian Liudong, Pan Shaopeng, Chen Xiangshan, et al., November 13.

Problem of the Foreign Merchant Plaintiff's Legal Person

In the case of the US merchant Aier Wulai Kaoer Burke Company suing William Wu for a debt dispute in the First District Court of the Special District, the court had ordered the accountant to investigate and report on the issue of account reconciliation between the two parties before the case could be reviewed. Yesterday, when the hearing was held, the plaintiff's lawyer Lu Dun stated first, followed by the defendant's agents, lawyers Li Fengshen and Zhao, who stood up to object, stating that the subject of the lawsuit still needed to be corrected. Because in the original complaint, the plaintiff filed the lawsuit in the name of the company. According to the law, a foreign legal person who has not registered with the Chinese government cannot enjoy the right to sue. The court must order the original complaint to be corrected before the trial can proceed. Because the plaintiff company is located in New York, USA, it will take several months to supplement and sign the complaint. Therefore, Judge Lou ruled that the plaintiff should supplement the corrected complaint within two months and then reopen the trial.

Yang Huchen Executes Legal Affairs

Mr. Yang Huchen, a native of Jiangsu, is over thirty years old and has studied law all his life and has a great understanding of it. Free Talk

Random Memories

— Yanzi

Song Qing's Sole Defense of Jinzhou

Since the Donglin Party Incident in Korea, Xiangcheng (Yuan Shikai), then a special envoy to Korea, rushed back. The Sino-Japanese war was thus unavoidable. Wu Dacheng, the governor of Hunan, volunteered to lead troops, stationed outside the customs. The imperial court appointed Song Qing, the Sichuan brigade general, as his deputy. Song was experienced in military affairs, having been under Feng Zicai, whose troops defeated the French army at Liangshan during the Sino-French War. His soldiers were well-trained and had been through many battles. At daybreak, the entire army would form ranks and enter the training ground to practice shooting. When the Wu army heard the gunfire, they suspected that the enemy army was breaking through their defenses, and the entire army collapsed. Song's camp was originally meant to provide flanking support, but it was almost affected. Song led his troops to retreat and garrison Jinzhou, strictly repairing defenses. The Japanese army dispatched large forces to besiege the city for months, using all sorts of methods, but to no avail. Song's troops were skilled at shooting, and their shots were always accurate. They ambushed and defended the city walls, killing over a thousand Japanese soldiers attacking the city. The Japanese army feared them like tigers. When the Treaty of Shimonoseki was concluded, the imperial court ordered Song to return to his post as Sichuan brigade general and lead his troops back to Sichuan. The gentry and people of Jinzhou tried to stop his carriage without success, and bid him farewell in the western suburbs. Halfway through the drinking, Song stood up and delivered a deeply felt speech of thanks. Everyone present was moved to tears. His war exploits are scattered among many people's writings. The people of Jinzhou still praise him to this day. He was truly a famous general in the Sino-Japanese War of 1894-95.

Buchaotingcao Zhaifu Talks

Franklin (Part 1)

One of the Biographies of Little Apprentices

Benjamin Franklin was born in 1706 and died in 1790, living to the age of eighty-four. After his death, his tombstone was inscribed with these lines: "He snatched power from the hands of emperors and electricity from the heavens."

This short epitaph is nothing less than a small reflection of Franklin's life, achievements, and scholarship. He was a politician, writer, and scientist. If you read his autobiography, you will be surprised to discover that this great man came from a humble background as a small apprentice. Everyone knows about his contributions to the American independence movement, so I don't need to say more. I just want to recount his small history as an apprentice and his contributions to science.

He entered a Latin elementary school at the age of eight, switched to an arithmetic and writing school at the age of nine, and dropped out of school at the age of ten due to financial difficulties. He followed his father to learn how to make candles and soap. He did not like this craft, but he was good at swimming and rowing and often wanted to go to sea. His father knew his inclinations and was very worried, so he often took him to visit carpenters, bricklayers, coppersmiths, winch makers, and other craftsmen on the street in order to choose a profession for life. This is a responsibility that all parents or teachers should fulfill. However, cursory visits are not very useful. We must guide children to look carefully, and only if they can do it after seeing it will it be effective. Franklin said in his autobiography that this kind of close and detailed visit had a great influence on him. Later, when things in the house were broken, he didn't need a craftsman, he could repair them himself, and if scientific experiments needed instruments, he could also make them himself. These skills all came from visiting craftsmen.

Although he was an apprentice in a candle shop, he liked to read. Two years later, his father asked him to learn printing because of this. In 1717, his brother James brought a printing press and type from England to set up a printing shop in Boston, and he was ordered by his father to sign a contract with James to be an apprentice for nine years. At this time, he was only twelve years old, and he would be twenty-one years old when the contract expired. Since he became an apprentice in the printing shop, he met many apprentices in bookstores, and the bookstores in the whole city became his circulating library. Whenever he borrowed a book, he had to finish reading it overnight, because according to the rules, he had to return it to the owner the next morning. In this way, although he was an apprentice, he was also a student, because he read several times more books than the students in ordinary schools.

Caricatures in Japanese Newspapers

— Zheng Yimei

Japan, with its small three islands, is insufficient to allow its people to thrive, and there is always the danger of volcanic eruptions and earthquakes. Therefore, it has strengthened its ambitions for aggression, and China, with its abundant products and vast territory, is the first to bear the brunt. Asking for and taking whatever it wants, it has achieved today's situation, which is not the result of just one morning or evening. I still remember the Sino-Japanese War. After the Japanese pirates occupied Korea, they were arrogant and looked down on everything. The Shishi Shinpo, a newspaper in their country at the time, once published a picture. The picture was of two goddesses holding wheels in battle, heroic and not yielding to men. This referred to Japan and England. In the middle of the two goddesses stood two children in adoration, referring to China and Korea. What was China's position? What was Korea's position? With absolutely unequal positions, the Japanese actually viewed them with the same eyes. Their desire to destroy China had been clearly revealed decades ago. Recently, since the September 18th Incident, the Japanese pirates have rampaged, burning, looting, killing, and doing everything imaginable. Every time they occupy a place, their newspapers noisily report it, thinking it is a great plan, and they issue extra editions to sell along the streets, like thunder. A certain newspaper even published a caricature, depicting a demon standing behind a child covered in wounds, while a man in a wide robe and wooden clogs holds a sword, killing the demon and comforting the child, like a father or elder brother to a younger sibling. Indeed, our country's warlords, fighting for power and profit, with endless wars, are a demon at work. China's internal and external troubles, with disasters occurring one after another, are nothing less than a body covered in wounds. Seeing this picture, how can we not be shocked? Will China willingly accept the protection of the Japanese? Or will we strive to protect ourselves? Our countrymen must decide. The moment of survival is at hand. How can we not be vigilant?

World Snippets

— Haike

Novel Alarm Clocks Westerners have to drink a cup of tea or coffee every morning. Wealthy men and women only have to open their eyes, and male and female servants will bring tea trays and let them drink comfortably in bed. As for ordinary bachelors who have no wives or servants, since no one wakes them up at the appropriate time, how can they have tea and coffee to drink? Therefore, they have to think of a way to save themselves. Recently, the Inventions Exhibition in London displayed a pair of novel alarm clocks. It is not known which inventor who sympathized with bachelors invented them. The function of this new alarm clock is not only to wake you up from your sleep, but also to make tea for you to drink. You only need to turn on the mechanism at night before going to bed, and at the prescribed time the next morning, the electric current will ignite the gas stove. A pot of water has already been placed on the stove, and tea leaves or coffee have been automatically placed in the teapot. After a while, the water in the pot boils and the tea is made. Then the bell rings loudly, not only urging you to get up, but also reporting that the tea is ready and you can get up to drink it. How convenient are these new inventions? They can truly be regarded as a bachelor's good helper.

Strange News of a Chaste Woman Committing Suicide After Being Jilted

— Sun Choucheng

I recently received a letter from a friend in Hangzhou, describing the strange event of a chaste woman committing suicide by hanging herself in Dongmuwu, near Liuxia. I am now transcribing it below.

Dongmuwu is located under Daling Mountain, with clear mountains and beautiful waters and tea trees everywhere. There are more than a hundred households. A certain Zhang plants dozens of acres of tea. His family is well-off. A woman from Ganxi, near Minwu, was married to him. She was quite beautiful and gentle. Zhang spent all day with her in the boudoir, unwilling to leave her for a moment. Over time, he became weak and frail. He died the following year, leaving his wife behind. At the time of the coffin, the woman wept bitterly over the corpse, wishing to die with him. She was stopped after being comforted by relatives. From then on, she abandoned cosmetics and spoke little, working diligently to raise her orphaned child. Therefore, everyone in the family regarded her as a chaste woman.

Because the woman had many fields and few people, she needed help. She hired a certain Shao from the same village as a long-term worker. Shao was young and strong and worked very diligently. He originally had a wife, but he sold her due to poverty and supported himself by working. When Zhang's wife died, she felt deep affection for her husband and was bound by the moral teachings, so she restrained herself and did not dare to be licentious. Later, she felt lonely and bitter, and there was no one to comfort her. Gradually, she became unwilling to sleep alone. Shao saw through her secret feelings and took the opportunity to seduce her. Over time, she was bewitched and fell in love with him. So they were master and servant by day and husband and wife by night, whispering sweet nothings to each other, regretting that they had not met sooner. But on the surface, they still wore the mask of chastity. Outsiders, seeing how deeply she loved her husband when he was in his coffin, did not suspect that she had changed her mind halfway through and continued to praise her.

Unexpectedly, Shao was insidious. He not only lusted after her beauty, but also coveted her wealth. When they first met, they vowed to be together. They worked tirelessly, hoping to win her favor. The woman had been parched for so long and finally received sweet rain, as if she had been anesthetized. Seeing that she had fallen into his trap, Shao made excuses to borrow money. The woman was afraid of displeasing him and obeyed his every command. After the money was exhausted, she continued with jewelry. After the jewelry was used up, she sold the field property. But the family's wealth was limited, and the desires were difficult to fill. For several years, all of Zhang's estate, both movable and immovable, was consumed by Shao alone. Then, because his repeated requests were not granted, he knew that the money had been exhausted. Shao then went away on some pretext, avoiding seeing her.

After losing her love, Zhang's wife tried to find Shao's whereabouts, hoping to continue their old love. She was like a drunkard all day long. Then, the black curtain of false chastity was torn down. The relatives' usual respect for her turned into contempt. She soon learned that Shao had found a new lover and was spending his honeymoon. Because the woman had been confused by him for several years, she had not only lost her body, but also lost her wealth. Her reputation was ruined. She was filled with regret and shame. She did not care about her face and went to Shao's house to question him. But Shao had heard the news and had fled far away with his new lover. At this point, Zhang's wife was in a dilemma and had the thought of being tired of the world. So she sneaked into Shao's house and hanged herself. In the evening, Shao returned and was greatly shocked by the sight. He asked someone to go to Ganxi to invite her mother. After mediation, a ceremony was held for three days, and he provided a coffin to atone for his past sins. Thus, the strange news of a chaste woman committing suicide after being jilted spread throughout the village.

A Record of Jade Purity and Ice Cleanliness

— Sun

Many of the capital's singers come from famous families. Because they are heartbroken by the difficulty of maintaining their purity and have suffered the pain of war and separation, they have no choice but to use the songs they learned in their boudoirs to sell their art to support their parents. This can also hurt themselves. As far as I know, the singer Ding Meiyu of Feilong Pavilion is from a prominent family in Qiantang, who lived in the Xizi Lake. Her father was a military officer and had made many military achievements. Unfortunately, due to a certain incident, he was imprisoned. From then on, the prison officers were respected, and the general's life was cheap. The iron windows were long at night, and there was little hope of release. Therefore, in addition to writing letters to redeem his sins, Meiyu also thought that her brother had not yet achieved fame and could not be burdened with the cost of rice, and that her mother was old and dared not seek a day's pleasure. Therefore, in a helpless situation, she made a plan for compromise. Fortunately, she had a skill in the pear garden, which was better than finding a fortune teller. So the whole family moved to Beijing, making a living by singing in the brothel. Although this matter is close to selling art, it is also equivalent to selling literature. There is no suspicion of licentious or transgressive behavior, and there is also the meaning of filial piety. My friend Tiankou Weng, in addition to listening to the songs, gave her a couplet: "Mulan feeds the horse, Ti Ying petitions the emperor, her virtues protect the sacred fungus, her kindness touches the Three Bamboo Compassionate Clouds, turning into the fragrance of a beautiful woman's herbs." "A robe of plain silk, a zither of flying jade, her jade face blooms like a full moon, willing to wash away the golden dust of the Six Dynasties, she is originally jade pure and ice clean."

Short News

— Xin Quan

The famous play "The Coiwinal Cold," written by the great playwright Martin Falevin, was performed on the New York stage for a year and won the coveted Drama League Award. It was then made into a film and transported to Shanghai, where it opened at the Nanjing Grand Theater. It has special features that the stage cannot have and is the most magical sad love film. Its layout is purely novelistic, emphasizing performance and plot, and there is not much dialogue. It can profoundly depict the pain of sacrificing love. The background is excellent. The jailbreak scene, with machine guns firing, is shocking and unparalleled. The great star Hess Deng plays the judge, who is extremely harsh and vividly portrayed. Philip Fomos plays Hanker, who is particularly rich in inner performance. The trial judge's daughter, Constance, also performs well. The other characters are all quite watchable. The director of this film, Hawke, is commendable for his faithful translation and for giving people a great stimulus.

Statement A section was omitted from the article "The Mother of Thought" the other day. It is now supplemented as follows.

"To walk without feeling difficulty is a mediocre person. To not even move one's feet but create thousands of difficulties in one's heart is a presumptuous person. To walk and feel difficulty and then want to solve this difficulty and not stop until the difficulty is solved is a scientist."

Rotary Club Story

The Country Bumpkin Goes to Shanghai Again (16)

— Bao Tianxiao

That black "Ce Lao" (ticket inspector) was wearing a suit of white clothes. With a black face, a pair of yellow eyes, and two rows of white teeth, he really looked like a ghost. The country bumpkin thought: This brother of Zhang Fei, elder brother of Zhou Cang, I wonder what he's doing on the tram? I'll have to take a closer look.

He saw that the "Ce Lao" got on the tram without saying a word, and checked the passengers' tickets one by one. Many passengers had different ways of keeping their little tickets. Some held them in their hands, some stuffed them in their hats, some clipped them in their ears, and some held them in their mouths. The "Ce Lao" silently checked them one by one, and then disappeared like a ghost.

"That's what they call a 'Ce Lao'." The country bumpkin figured he'd learned another trick today.

"Sanma Road is here, please get off." This was the ticket seller giving a special greeting to the country bumpkin. Otherwise, ticket sellers never announce the stops to passengers. If you miss your stop, it's none of their business, and you have to pay for an extra ticket.

And when the country bumpkin got off the tram, he even pointed him in a direction and said, "Walk west, it's not many shops, it's the Grand Theater." After saying that, the tram went ding-ding-dang-dang and headed south again.

The country bumpkin listened to the ticket seller's directions and indeed walked west a few steps. By then it was already evening, and the electric lights on the road were shining brightly. Cars, carriages, rickshaws, bicycles, collapsible carts, and small carts were all squeezing the pedestrians. The country bumpkin managed to squeeze through, and he soon saw the three large characters "Grand Theater." Now he couldn't help but hesitate. He still remembered that his nephew A-Mulin had told him he was in the Meilan Lane in the French Concession, so how had he ended up at the Grand Theater? He had no idea if this place was the French Concession, so how did they say A-Mulin was here? And my photo is across from the Grand Theater?

At this time, the Grand Theater was in the middle of seating, and many men and women with syphilis (Note 5) were entering the theater one after another. There was also a group of "anmu" (ticket touts) carrying stacks of theater programs. When they saw someone walking from afar at the entrance, they didn't care if they were coming to see the show or not and shouted in unison. When they saw someone wearing glasses, they would shout: "Glasses! Glasses! Someone with glasses is coming!" When they saw someone wearing a long gown, they would call: "Long gown! Long gown! Someone in a long gown is coming!" Whoever shouted first would go to greet them, and they would be considered their customer.

The country bumpkin was looking around when the touts thought he was also coming to see the show. One of the touts coughed:

"A-Mulin! A-Mulin! A-Mulin is here!" As he spoke, he winked at the person next to him.

The country bumpkin was very surprised. He thought his nephew was really here.

(Note 5) In recent times, those who satirize Mei Lanfang call him Mei Du (梅毒, which sounds like "syphilis").

Commercial News

Financial: Gold Prices Soar

Short Covering Due to Approaching Settlement

The gold price continued its rapid rise. Yesterday, the 13th, the benchmark gold price again showed a sharp increase, with volatile waves. There was no firm grip on the market, with both rising and falling periods. There were a total of 22 taels recalled from the previous market, ultimately rebounding by more than 20 taels. This was mainly due to the approaching settlement date, with the bulls trying to push the price higher and the shorts having to cover their positions. Furthermore, the scarce inventory of physical gold contributed to a bullish sentiment among dealers, resulting in demand exceeding supply in the market. The silver market report did not have any impact, likely because the European market turned soft, and Citibank had been selling. Therefore, the market opened high, then weakened slightly, before rising again. As for foreign exchange, it was apparently loose but secretly tight, eventually exceeding 610 taels, but with fluctuations, hovering around 10 taels. The after-market once reached beyond 20 taels, but unexpectedly, a sudden storm arose. The exchange rate rose and then fell, with sellers on the floor acting swiftly. Rumors of escalating conflict in the Heilongjiang province caused a plunge of 10 taels, eventually stabilizing at the end.

A Frenzied Jump at the Opening

The market jumped wildly from the very beginning, rising 13.7 mace to 606.5 taels. The large silver bars rose another 11/16, and forward silver rose 6/8. The silver price increased by 7/8, but buyers were satisfied and unmoved. The Ningbo guild, as well as Tongtaichang, Fuyu, and others, were selling. The price then dropped from 607 taels to 600 taels, followed by a rebound of 6 taels, as Hengchangyong and others bought in, and the exchange rate appeared firm. The closing exchange rate for U.S. dollars was 36.875 to 36.75, and for British pounds it was initially 11 pence 4375. Then, banks absorbed at the same price. However, the posted rate for British pounds had already increased by 1 pence, and the U.S. dollar by 1.5 yuan. This was due to the small exchange rate reported between the U.K. and the U.S. At 02:30, Fuyu, Fuchang, Yuanxing, Yongqian, Changxiang, and others all entered the market, and HSBC also bought British pounds for December at 11 pence 4375. As a result, the gold price soared, increasing by 10 and 9.5/100ths taels, to 13.5 taels. In an instant, within ten minutes, it plunged 6 taels, because British pounds for February were still settling at 375. In addition, Hengyu, Zhifengyong, Tongtaichang, Shunli, and others sold until 10:00, reaching 607.5 mace. After entering the market, it rose more than 4 taels, almost with British pound banks mutually doing 3125, and the U.S. dollar at 36.5 yuan. Especially Hengxing, Yuanwanxing, Shunli, Tianfengyong, Yongchengfengyong, and others were competing to buy, reaching 11.8 taels around 11:00. Suddenly, news of intense fighting in the Northeast caused all parties to sell vigorously, plunging 7 taels in just three or four minutes to 605 taels. The selling frenzy began to subside after entering the market, with Chengfengyong, Hengxing, Yuangan, Changxiang, Yuanxingyong, and the Ningbo guild entering the market in succession. As the exchange market also turned favorable, the price soared more than 10 taels, reaching 18.5 taels at noon. At the closing bell, the quoted price was changed to 662 taels, with a total fluctuation of around 50 taels.

The market opened high, at 20 taels, then 22 taels, which was the after-effect of the noon close. In an instant, the falling trend arose again. At 2:40, Zhifengyong, Fuchang, Shunli, Hengchangyong and others sold, and Huabi bought U.S. dollars for January at 36.25 yuan. At 4:00, it was only counted at 10 taels, and then there were zero-lot buyers coming in, rising three or four taels. When the market closed at 4:30, it was 13 taels and 7 mace, which was an increase of 20 and 9/100ths taels compared to the previous day, and was again raised to 15 taels. Goods were dragged in. If it were more visible when foreign wheat was smoothly settled, the impact would be even more considerable. The market was still low but only fell by about 2 fen compared to the previous day, but the sentiment for the distant period was relatively weaker (the lowest price for April was 2.05 taels). When the market opened in the afternoon, the gold market rebounded, and the Nanyang gang still absorbed slightly. The near and far terms rose by one or two fen compared to the morning. As a result, the current month did not move, November was up by 5 li, December was up by 5 li, March was up by 2.5 li, and April was down by 5 li, it is said.

Wheat: Soft in the Morning, Stable at Noon

Yesterday, after the opening of the futures wheat market in the morning, each month again tended to be sluggish, as the price of foreign wheat fell by about six, seven, or eight jiao. This kind of state seemed to contradict the expectations of most people. Because the gold market was unstable, people inside and outside the industry felt increasingly indifferent. The opening price for the current month immediately decreased to 3.65 taels, and the distant term was also decreased by 3 to 4 fen or so. However, the actual goods were not smooth, so the market atmosphere relied on this to be stable. When the market opened in the afternoon, the soaring gold market also saw sentiment rebound. Because most of those who settled foreign wheat at a time of unrest did not dare to observe and dump their holdings, and the scarcity of goods being dumped was not difficult to imagine. Therefore, in the subsequent steps, it may be possible to see the market stabilize for the time being because of this. As a result, the current month was down by 2 fen compared to the previous day, December was up by 1 fen, January was up by 2 fen, and March and April were down by 1 fen, it is said.

Zhabei Goods, Copper Coins, Bubble Coins Have Already Been Released

The Quanzhou large bubble Gui yuan coins were previously due to the fact that the return prices of various firms were too outrageous, and the two sides had been in stalemate for nearly a week. Recently, they have gradually approached, and yesterday it was heard that half of the upstream had been released, smaller by three taels or so compared to before, but the price was better than before it was released by one or two taels. However, according to the Quanzhou telegraph, the land price was unable to relax, and the market may be able to turn stable, it is said.

Silk and Tea: No Major Changes in Overseas Silk Market

There is Trading but No Market… Truly Lacking New News to Record

The overseas raw silk market is affected by economic unease. Raw silk factories have no sales, and silk prices have no major changes, and are of the variety that have trades but no market. Recently, in January, the New York market has had Standard period silk (i.e. Japanese silk) on the silk exchange fluctuate by a few American cents per pound, with no fluctuations in silk prices. The depression of the Chinese and foreign silk markets is at its extreme, and there is truly a lack of new news to record, it is said.

Tunxi Zhen Mei Has Already Been Motivated

Since the invasion of the Eastern provinces by the violent Japanese army, the foreign tea market in this port has shown a steep decline due to the serious situation and the soaring leading rate. In recent days, Pingshui Zhucha and Luzhuang Zhenmei green tea have had sporadic sales. Yesterday, Tunxi Zhenmei, Tongfu, Jinlong, Xiehe and other firms all showed a trend of movement, and the price was opened at 80-90 taels, 2-3 taels lower than before. The market already has movement, but Wuyuan Gaozhuang goods are still sluggish, it is said.

Cloth: Velvet Goods Exceptionally Active

Velvet goods

Hardware Industry Competes by Cutting Prices

Yesterday, hardware transactions were quite sluggish. Although various businesses in the industry tried their best to lower prices and peddle their goods everywhere, they were ultimately exhausted due to the large amount of goods and slow sales. Moreover, with a continuous supply and increasing inventory, morale is low. Therefore, the future trend seems uncertain. However, if the supply of tinplate, black iron sheet, and white iron tile runs out and there is a slight breakthrough, the market may regain a better outlook.

Social News

Gu Angru Translates Marshal Foch's European War Diary

I also requested General Haller, the commander-in-chief of the Polish army, to allow the Polish First Division to participate in the offensive.

As such, thanks to the efforts of all the officers and soldiers, the Laurence offensive was quickly and properly arranged. The 28th Infantry Division and the 3rd Cavalry Division, under the cover of a large artillery corps and 600 tanks, were prepared to launch an offensive on November 14th. The battle line was 20 miles long and would be closely connected to the fiercely bombarded 200-mile battle line. However, this front had new objectives but no strong enemy, so it was expected to conquer dozens of miles in one battle. Beyond this lay a desolate disaster area, which greatly hindered the Allied advance. The troops in this direction could then join forces to attack, in order to advance on the Rhine and directly attack Berlin. If our army advanced along this route, the final victory of the war could be secured.

At the beginning of November, the line from Valenciennes to Ghent and the Scheldt River formed the barrier of the Allied left wing, while the strong defenses of the Selle River on the Chambrai front formed the barrier of our central forces.

The American First Army and the French Fourth Army advanced on the left bank of the Meuse River, which was enough to outflank the Selle River line from the east. The French First Army and the British right wing attacked the line of the Scheldt River from the south, north of the Sensée River. The French Flanders Army Group took Ghent from the north.

I anticipated important developments in the north, so I moved my headquarters from Bombon to Saint-Lyé on October 18th. Now, it was only necessary to proceed uninterruptedly according to the predetermined strategy. The stalemate that our army had been forced into came to an end at the end of October.

From November 1st to 5th, the American First Army and the French Fourth Army successfully outflanked and advanced to the line of Les Islettes-Buzancy-Stonne. The British right wing, under the cover of the Deprez corps, also advanced to Iwuy-Philippeville. On the 5th and 6th, our army completely occupied the line of the Selle River.

I had a consultation with Marshal Haig about this. I asked him that when the British right wing advanced, he should withdraw the British Second Army, which was temporarily attached to the Flanders Army Group, to take charge of the left wing and redeploy his forces. I told him that if he wanted the Flanders Army Group to succeed, the British Second Army could not be moved until it had recovered Belgium up to the Scheldt River.

In fact, the Flanders Army Group had already reached the upper reaches of the Scheldt River and Ghent on November 1st, and the British Second Army was transferred back to Marshal Haig on November 4th. I then notified King Albert of Belgium on November 2nd.

After several victories, the French Flanders Army Group had advanced to the upper reaches of the Scheldt River and Ghent. In the future, the main battle for attacking the Scheldt River defense line would be undertaken by the British army southwest of Valenciennes. Therefore, all British troops should be under the command of the British Commander-in-Chief. Marshal Foch earnestly requested King Albert to transfer the British Second Army back to Marshal Haig's direct command from November 4th.

At that time, in view of the victory of the French First Army between October 24th and 27th, I wrote to Marshal Haig on October 27th, saying,

"The Deprez corps is progressing smoothly. The main force of the British army can contact the French First Army to attack towards the objectives of Mons, Iwuy, and La Chaussée."

On October 29th, Marshal Haig ordered his Fourth, Third, and Thirteenth Corps to prepare to attack again on November 3rd, but the attack only began on the 4th. The French First Army provided cover, resulting in a complete victory.

The German army was repeatedly wounded, and with the continuous advance of the French and American armies on the left wing, the German defense line wavered. On the 5th, a large-scale retreat began between the Mons Canal and the Esnes River. After this, the Meuse River front also wavered.

On the 8th, the Franco-Belgian forces of the Flanders Army Group occupied the crossings of the Scheldt River between Eecke and Audenarde. Hearing the news, the enemy troops retreated even more fiercely. The enemy had implemented a general retreat from the Dutch border to Haute-Sambre on the Meuse River.

The Allied forces pursued closely, hoping to take the Rhine River in one fell swoop and disintegrate the enemy forces, due to the natural barrier of the Rhine River.

Page 18

The German government is now preparing to negotiate on the basis of President Wilson's speech to Congress on January 8, 1918, and subsequent speeches such as that on September 27, 1918. Finally, the German government, due to the urgent domestic situation, requested the conclusion of an immediate armistice treaty on land, sea, and air.

President Wilson issued a reply on October 8th, arguing that the immediate withdrawal of German troops from the occupied areas should be a prerequisite for the conclusion of an armistice treaty.

On the same day (October 8th), I first voluntarily notified Mr. Clemenceau of the obligations that the enemy army should bear. These obligations were based on the following three principles:

If the following conditions are not accepted, there will be no ceasefire for the troops within Belgium and France.

1. Restore countries that have been occupied in violation of international law, such as Belgium, France, Alsace-Lorraine, and Luxembourg, and return their residents. As the enemy army must withdraw within 15 days and immediately send residents back to their hometowns, this is the first condition for the armistice.

2. Our army must guarantee the occupation of a considerable military starting point base in preparation for resuming the war and annihilating the enemy in the event of a breakdown of peace negotiations. Our army must occupy two or three bridgeheads on the Rhine River (the bridgeheads must form a semicircle on the right bank, with a radius of 18 and 3/4 miles). This must also be implemented within 15 days, which is the second condition for the armistice.

3. Occupy collateral for compensation. The amount of compensation will be proposed during peace negotiations. Therefore, the enemy army must withdraw from the left bank of the Rhine River within 30 days, and the Allied forces will occupy it and manage it jointly with the local authorities until the conclusion of the peace treaty. This is the third condition for the armistice.

There are also additional conditions as follows:

4. Military equipment that the German army cannot remove within the time limit must be left behind and not destroyed.

5. Troops that cannot be fully withdrawn within the time limit must be disarmed and considered prisoners of war.

6. Railway materials must be left behind and not destroyed. All vehicles occupied in Belgium and France should be returned immediately.

7. All military buildings │barracks, arsenals, munitions factories│ must be maintained as they are and left behind, and no objects should be taken away or destroyed.

8. The same applies to industrial buildings and various factories.

9. The war will cease within 24 hours after the above conditions are approved by the contracting countries. (To be continued)

Social News Submission Guidelines

(1) The text should be about domestic and foreign science, industry, commerce, rural areas.

(2) News on hygiene, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life. Pictures are limited to various lyrical paintings about social life.

(3) Photos of seasons, landscapes, animals and plants, people, and news photography are acceptable. Photos of ladies in seasonal landscape photography are especially welcome.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(5) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, do not write in a sloppy manner, and save Western text where possible. If you must use the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not draw pictures with blue ink, and do not use colored paper. Use limited paper black drawing.
